CATRIONA 

 DEDICATION . 

 to 
 CHARLES BAXTER , Writer to the Signet . 

 my Dear Charles , 

 it be the fate of sequel to disappoint those who have wait for they ; and my David , have be leave to kick his heel for more than a lustre in the British Linen Company s office , must expect his late re - appearance to be greet with hoot , if not with missile . yet , when I remember the day of our exploration , I be not without hope . there should be leave in our native city some seed of the elect ; some long - legged , hot - head youth must repeat to - day our dream and wandering of so many year ago ; he will relish the pleasure , which should have be ours , to follow among name street and number house the country walk of David Balfour , to identify Dean , and Silvermills , and Broughton , and Hope Park , and Pilrig , and poor old Lochend if it still be stand , and the Figgate Whins if there be any of they leave ; or to push   on a long holiday   so far afield as Gillane or the Bass . so , perhaps , his eye shall be open to behold the series of the generation , and he shall weigh with surprise his momentous and nugatory gift of life . 

 you be still as when first I see , as when I last address you in the venerable city which I must always think of as my home . and I have come so far ; and the sight and thought of my youth pursue I ; and I see like a vision the youth of my father , and of his father , and the whole stream of life flow down there far in the north , with the sound of laughter and tear , to cast I out in the end , as by a sudden freshet , on these ultimate island . and I admire and bow my head before the romance of destiny . 

 R. L. S. 

 Vailima , Upolu , 
 Samoa , 1892 . 

 CATRIONA Part I the LORD ADVOCATE 

 CHAPTER I a BEGGAR on HORSEBACK 

 the 25th day of August , 1751 , about two in the afternoon , I , David Balfour , come forth of the British Linen Company , a porter attend I with a bag of money , and some of the chief of these merchant bow I from their door . two day before , and even so late as yestermorning , I be like a beggar - man by the wayside , clothe in rag , bring down to my last shilling , my companion a condemn traitor , a price set on my own head for a crime with the news of which the country ring . to - day I be serve heir to my position in life , a land laird , a bank porter by I carry my gold , recommendation in my pocket , and   in the word of the saying   the ball directly at my foot . 

 there be two circumstance that serve I as ballast to so much sail . the first be the very difficult and deadly business I have still to handle ; the second , the place that I be in . the tall , black city , and the number and movement and noise of so many folk , make a new world for I , after the moorland braes , the sea - sand and the still country - side that I have frequent up to then . the throng of the citizen in particular abash I . Rankeillor s son be short and small in the girth ; his clothe scarce hold on I ; and it be plain I be ill qualified to strut in the front of a bank - porter . it be plain , if I do so , I should but set folk laughing , and   what be bad in my case   set they ask question . so that I behoove to come by some clothe of my own , and in the meanwhile to walk by the porter s side , and put my hand on his arm as though we be a pair of friend . 

 at a merchant s in the luckenbooth I have myself fit out : none too fine , for I have no idea to appear like a beggar on horseback ; but comely and responsible , so that servant should respect I . thence to an armour s , where I get a plain sword , to suit with my degree in life . I feel safe with the weapon , though   for one so ignorant of defence   it might be call an add danger . the porter , who be naturally a man of some experience , judge my accoutrement to be well choose . 

 " naethe kenspeckle , "   1   say he ; " plain , dacent clae . as for the rapier , nae doubt it sit wi your degree ; but an I have be you , I would have waire my sill well - gate than that . " and he propose I should buy winter - hosen from a wife in the cowgate - back , that be a cousin of his own , and make they " extraordinar endurable . " 

 but I have other matter on my hand more pressing . here I be in this old , black city , which be for all the world like a rabbit - warren , not only by the number of its indweller , but the complication of its passage and hole . it be , indeed , a place where no strange have a chance to find a friend , let be another stranger . suppose he even to hit on the right close , people dwelt so thronged in these tall house , he might very well seek a day before he chance on the right door . the ordinary course be to hire a lad they call a caddie , who be like a guide or pilot , lead you where you have occasion , and   your errand be do   bring you again where you be lodge . but these caddy , be always employ in the same sort of service , and have it for obligation to be well informed of every house and person in the city , have grow to form a brotherhood of spy ; and I know from tale of Mr. Campbell s how they communicate one with another , what a rage of curiosity they conceive as to their employer s business , and how they be like eye and finger to the police . it would be a piece of little wisdom , the way I be now place , to take such a ferret to my tail . I have three visit to make , all immediately needful : to my kinsman Mr. Balfour of Pilrig , to Stewart the writer that be Appin s agent , and to William Grant Esquire of Prestongrange , Lord Advocate of Scotland . Mr. Balfour s be a non - committal visit ; and besides   Pilrig be in the country   I make bold to find the way to it myself , with the help of my two leg and a Scots tongue . but the rest be in a different case . not only be the visit to appin s agent , in the midst of the cry about the Appin murder , dangerous in itself , but it be highly inconsistent with the other . I be like to have a bad enough time of it with my Lord Advocate Grant , the good of way ; but to go to he hot - foot from Appin s agent , be little likely to mend my own affair , and might prove the mere ruin of friend Alan s. the whole thing , besides , give I a look of run with the hare and hunting with the hound that be little to my fancy . I determine , therefore , to be do at once with Mr. Stewart and the whole Jacobitical side of my business , and to profit for that purpose by the guidance of the porter at my side . but it chance I have scarce give he the address , when there come a sprinkle of rain nothing to hurt , only for my new clothe and we take shelter under a pend at the head of a close or alley . 

 be strange to what I see , I step a little far in . the narrow paved way descend swiftly . prodigious tall house spring upon each side and bulge out , one storey beyond another , as they rise . at the top only a ribbon of sky show in . by what I could spy in the window , and by the respectable person that pass out and in , I see the house to be very well occupy ; and the whole appearance of the place interested I like a tale . 

 I be still gaze , when there come a sudden brisk tramp of foot in time and clash of steel behind I . turn quickly , I be aware of a party of armed soldier , and , in their midst , a tall man in a great coat . he walk with a stoop that be like a piece of courtesy , genteel and insinuating : he wave his hand plausibly as he go , and his face be sly and handsome . I think his eye take I in , but could not meet it . this procession go by to a door in the close , which a serve - man in a fine livery set open ; and two of the soldier - lad carry the prisoner within , the rest linger with their firelock by the door . 

 there can nothing pass in the street of a city without some following of idle folk and child . it be so now ; but the more part melt away incontinent until but three be leave . one be a girl ; she be dress like a lady , and have a screen of the Drummond colour on her head ; but her comrade or   I should say   follower be ragged gillie , such as I have see the match of by the dozen in my Highland journey . they all speak together earnestly in Gaelic , the sound of which be pleasant in my ear for the sake of Alan ; and , though the rain be by again , and my porter pluck at I to be go , I even draw nearer where they be , to listen . the lady scold sharply , the other make apology and cringe before she , so that I make sure she be come of a chief s house . all the while the three of they seek in their pocket , and by what I could make out , they have the matter of half a farthing among the party ; which make I smile a little to see all Highland folk alike for fine obeisance and empty sporran . 

 it chance the girl turn suddenly about , so that I see her face for the first time . there be no great wonder than the way the face of a young woman fit in a man s mind , and stay there , and he could never tell you why ; it just seem it be the thing he want . she have wonderful bright eye like star , and I daresay the eye have a part in it ; but what I remember the most clearly be the way her lip be a trifle open as she turn . and , whatever be the cause , I stand there star like a fool . on her side , as she have not know there be anyone so near , she look at I a little long , and perhaps with more surprise , than be entirely civil . 

 it go through my country head she might be wonder at my new clothe ; with that , I blush to my hair , and at the sight of my colouring it be to be suppose she draw her own conclusion , for she move her gillie far down the close , and they fall again to this dispute , where I could hear no more of it . 

 I have often admire a lassie before then , if scarce so sudden and strong ; and it be rather my disposition to withdraw than to come forward , for I be much in fear of mockery from the womenkind . you would have think I have now all the more reason to pursue my common practice , since I have meet this young lady in the city street , seemingly follow a prisoner , and accompany with two very ragged indecent - like highlandman . but there be here a different ingredient ; it be plain the girl think I have be pry in her secret ; and with my new clothe and sword , and at the top of my new fortune , this be more than I could swallow . the beggar on horseback could not bear to be thrust down so low , or , at least of it , not by this young lady . 

 I follow , accordingly , and take off my new hat to she the good that I be able . 

 " Madam , " say I , " I think it only fair to myself to let you understand I have no Gaelic . it be true I be listen , for I have friend of my own across the Highland line , and the sound of that tongue come friendly ; but for your private affair , if you have speak Greek , I might have have more guess at they . " 

 she make I a little , distant curtsey . " there be no harm do , " say she , with a pretty accent , most like the English   but more agreeable . " a cat may look at a king . " 

 " I do not mean to offend , " say I. " I have no skill of city manner ; I never before this day set foot inside the door of Edinburgh . take I for a country lad it s what I be ; and I would rather I tell you than you find it out . " 

 " indeed , it will be a very unusual thing for stranger to be speak to each other on the causeway , " she reply . " but if you be landward   2   breed it will be different . I be as landward as yourself ; I be Highland , as you see , and think myself the far from my home . " 

 " it be not yet a week since I pass the line , " say I. " Less than a week ago I be on the braes of Balwhidder . " 

 " Balwhither ? " she cry . " come ye from Balwhither ! the name of it make all there be of I rejoice . you will not have be long there , and not know some of our friend or family ? " 

 " I live with a very honest , kind man call Duncan Dhu Maclaren , " I reply . 

 " well , I know Duncan , and you give he the true name ! " she say ; " and if he be an honest man , his wife be honest indeed . " 

 " ay , " say I , " they be fine people , and the place be a bonny place . " 

 " where in the great world be such another ! " she cry ; " I be love the smell of that place and the root that grow there . " 

 I be infinitely take with the spirit of the maid . " I could be wish I have bring you a spray of that heather , " say I. " and , though I do ill to speak with you at the first , now it seem we have common acquaintance , I make it my petition you will not forget I . David Balfour be the name I be know by . this be my lucky day , when I have just come into a land estate , and be not very long out of a deadly peril . I wish you would keep my name in mind for the sake of Balwhidder , " say I , " and I will yours for the sake of my lucky day . " 

 " my name be not speak , " she reply , with a great deal of haughtiness . " More than a hundred year it have not go upon man s tongue , save for a blink . I be nameless , like the Folk of Peace .   3   Catriona Drummond be the one I use . " 

 now indeed I know where I be stand . in all broad Scotland there be but the one name proscribe , and that be the name of the Macgregors . yet so far from flee this undesirable acquaintancy , I plunge the deep in . 

 " I have be sit with one who be in the same case with yourself , " say I , " and I think he will be one of your friend . they call he Robin Oig . " 

 " do ye so ? " cry she . " Ye meet Rob ? " 

 " I pass the night with he , " say I. 

 " he be a fowl of the night , " say she . 

 " there be a set of pipe there , " I go on , " so you may judge if the time pass . " 

 " you should be no enemy , at all event , " say she . " that be his brother there a moment since , with the red soldier round he . it be he that I call father . " 

 " be it so ? " cry I. " be you a daughter of James More s ? " 

 " all the daughter that he have , " say she : " the daughter of a prisoner ; that I should forget it so , even for one hour , to talk with stranger ! " 

 here one of the gillie address she in what he have of English , to know what " she "   meaning by that himself   be to do about " ta sneeshin . " I take some note of he for a short , bandy - legged , red - haired , big - headed man , that I be to know more of to my cost . 

 " there can be none the day , Neil , " she reply . " how will you get sneeshin , want siller ! it will teach you another time to be more careful ; and I think James More will not be very well pleased with Neil of the Tom . " 

 " Miss Drummond , " I say , " I tell you I be in my lucky day . here I be , and a bank - porter at my tail . and remember I have have the hospitality of your own country of Balwhidder . " 

 " it be not one of my people give it , " say she . 

 " ah , well , " say I , " but I be owe your uncle at least for some spring upon the pipe . besides which , I have offer myself to be your friend , and you have be so forgetful that you do not refuse I in the proper time . " 

 " if it have be a great sum , it might have do you honour , " say she ; " but I will tell you what this be . James More lie shackle in prison ; but this time past they will be bring he down here daily to the Advocate s. . . . " 

 " the Advocate s ! " I cry . " be that . . . ? " 

 " it be the house of the Lord Advocate Grant of Prestongrange , " say she . " there they bring my father one time and another , for what purpose I have no thought in my mind ; but it seem there be some hope dawn for he . all this same time they will not let I be see he , nor yet he write ; and we wait upon the King s street to catch he ; and now we give he his snuff as he go by , and now something else . and here be this son of trouble , Neil , son of Duncan , have lose my four - penny piece that be to buy that snuff , and James More must go want , and will think his daughter have forget he . " 

 I take sixpence from my pocket , give it to Neil , and bid he go about his errand . then to she , " that sixpence come with I by Balwhidder , " say I. 

 " ah ! " she say , " you be a friend to the Gregara ! " 

 " I would not like to deceive you , either , " say I. " I know very little of the Gregara and less of James More and his doing , but since the while I have be stand in this close , I seem to know something of yourself ; and if you will just say a friend to Miss Catriona I will see you be the less cheated . " 

 " the one can not be without the other , " say she . 

 " I will even try , " say I. 

 " and what will you be think of myself ! " she cry , " to be hold my hand to the first stranger ! " 

 " I be think nothing but that you be a good daughter , " say I. 

 " I must not be without repay it , " she say ; " where be it you stop ! " 

 " to tell the truth , I be stop nowhere yet , " say I , " be not full three hour in the city ; but if you will give I your direction , I will be so bold as come seek my sixpence for myself . " 

 " will I can trust you for that ? " she ask . 

 " you need have little fear , " say I. 

 " James More could not bear it else , " say she . " I stop beyond the village of Dean , on the north side of the water , with Mrs. Drummond - Ogilvy of Allardyce , who be my near friend and will be glad to thank you . " 

 " you be to see I , then , so soon as what I have to do permit , " say I ; and , the remembrance of Alan roll in again upon my mind , I make haste to say farewell . 

 I could not but think , even as I do so , that we have make extraordinary free upon short acquaintance , and that a really wise young lady would have show herself more backward . I think it be the bank - porter that put I from this ungallant train of thought . 

 " I thoucht ye have be a lad of some kind o sense , " he begin , shoot out his lip . " ye re no likely to gang far this gate . a fule and his sill s shune part . eh , but ye re a green callant ! " he cry , " an a veecious , tae ! Cleikin up wi baubeejoe ! " 

 " if you dare to speak of the young lady . . . " I begin . 

 " Leddy ! " he cry . " haud we and safe us , whatten leddy ? can thon a leddy ? the toun s fu o they . leddie ! man , its weel see ye re no very acquant in Embro ! " 

 a clap of anger take I . 

 " here , " say I , " lead I where I tell you , and keep your foul mouth shut ! " 

 he do not wholly obey I , for , though he no more address I directly , he very impudent sing at I as he go in a manner of innuendo , and with an exceedingly ill voice and ear 

 " as Mally Lee cam doun the street , her capuchin do flee , 
 she cuist a look ahint she to see her negligee . 
 and we re a gaun east and wast , we re a gann ajee , 
 we re a gaun east and wast courtin Mally Lee . " 

 CHAPTER II the HIGHLAND WRITER 

 Mr. Charles Stewart the Writer dwelt at the top of the long stair ever mason set a hand to ; fifteen flight of it , no less ; and when I have come to his door , and a clerk have open it , and tell I his master be within , I have scarce breath enough to send my porter pack . 

 " Awa east and west wi ye ! " say I , take the money bag out of his hand , and follow the clerk in . 

 the outer room be an office with the clerk s chair at a table spread with law paper . in the inner chamber , which open from it , a little brisk man sit pore on a deed , from which he scarce raise his eye on my entrance ; indeed , he still keep his finger in the place , as though prepare to show I out and fall again to his study . this please I little enough ; and what please I less , I think the clerk be in a good posture to overhear what should pass between we . 

 I ask if he be Mr. Charles Stewart the Writer . 

 " the same , " say he ; " and , if the question be equally fair , who may you be yourself ? " 

 " you never hear tell of my name nor of I either , " say I , " but I bring you a token from a friend that you know well . that you know well , " I repeat , lower my voice , " but maybe be not just so keen to hear from at this present being . and the bit of business that I have to propone to you be rather in the nature of be confidential . in short , I would like to think we be quite private . " 

 he rise without more word , cast down his paper like a man ill - pleased , send forth his clerk of an errand , and shut to the house - door behind he . 

 " now , sir , " say he , return , " speak out your mind and fear nothing ; though before you begin , " he cry out , " I tell you mine misgive I ! I tell you beforehand , ye re either a Stewart or a Stewart send ye . a good name it be , and one it would ill - become my father s son to lightly . but I begin to grue at the sound of it . " 

 " my name be call Balfour , " say I , " David Balfour of Shaws . as for he that send I , I will let his token speak . " and I show the silver button . 

 " put it in your pocket , sir ! " cry he . " ye need name no name . the deevil s buckie , I ken the button of he ! and de il hae t ! where be he now ! " 

 I tell he I know not where Alan be , but he have some sure place   or think he have   about the north side , where he be to lie until a ship be find for he ; and how and where he have appoint to be speak with . 

 " it s be always my opinion that I would hang in a tow for this family of mine , " he cry , " and , dod ! I believe the day s come now ! get a ship for he , quot he ! and who s to pay for it ? the man s daft ! " 

 " that be my part of the affair , Mr. Stewart , " say I. " here be a bag of good money , and if more be want , more be to be have where it come from . " 

 " I needn t ask your politic , " say he . 

 " ye need not , " say I , smile , " for I m as big a Whig as grow . " 

 " stop a bit , stop a bit , " say Mr. Stewart . " what s all this ? a Whig ? then why be you here with Alan s button ? and what kind of a black - foot traffic be this that I find ye out in , Mr. Whig ? here be a forfeit rebel and an accuse murderer , with two hundred pound on his life , and ye ask I to meddle in his business , and then tell I ye re a Whig ! I have no mind of any such whig before , though I ve ken plenty of they . " 

 " he s a forfeited rebel , the more s the pity , " say I , " for the man s my friend . I can only wish he have be well guide . and an accuse murderer , that he be too , for his misfortune ; but wrongfully accuse . " 

 " I hear you say so , " say Stewart . 

 " More than you be to hear I say so , before long , " say I. " Alan Breck be innocent , and so be James . " 

 " oh ! " say he , " the two case hang together . if Alan be out , James can never be in . " 

 Hereupon I tell he briefly of my acquaintance with Alan , of the accident that bring I present at the Appin murder , and the various passage of our escape among the heather , and my recovery of my estate . " so , sir , you have now the whole train of these event , " I go on , " and can see for yourself how I come to be so much mingle up with the affair of your family and friend , which   for all of our sake   I wish have be plainer and less bloody . you can see for yourself , too , that I have certain piece of business depending , which be scarcely fit to lay before a lawyer choose at random . no more remain , but to ask if you will undertake my service ? " 

 " I have no great mind to it ; but come as you do with Alan s button , the choice be scarcely leave I , " say he . " what be your instruction ? " he add , and take up his pen . 

 " the first point be to smuggle Alan forth of this country , " say I , " but I need not be repeat that . " 

 " I be little likely to forget it , " say Stewart . 

 " the next thing be the bit money I be owe to Cluny , " I go on . " it would be ill for I to find a conveyance , but that should be no stick to you . it be two pound five shilling and three - halfpence farthe sterling . " 

 he note it . 

 " then , " say I , " there s a Mr. Henderland , a licensed preacher and missionary in Ardgour , that I would like well to get some snuff into the hand of ; and , as I daresay you keep touch with your friend in Appin   so near by , it s a job you could doubtless overtake with the other . " 

 " how much snuff be we to say ? " he ask . 

 " I be think of two pound , " say I. 

 " Two , " say he . 

 " then there s the lass Alison Hastie , in Lime Kilns , " say I. " she that help Alan and I across the Forth . I be think if I could get she a good Sunday gown , such as she could wear with decency in her degree , it would be an ease to my conscience ; for the mere truth be , we owe she our two life . " 

 " I be glad so see you be thrifty , Mr. Balfour , " say he , make his note . 

 " I would think shame to be otherwise the first day of my fortune , " say I. " and now , if you will compute the outlay and your own proper charge , I would be glad to know if I could get some spending - money back . it s not that I grudge the whole of it to get Alan safe ; it s not that I lack more ; but have draw so much the one day , I think it would have a very ill appearance if I be back again seek , the next . only be sure you have enough , " I add , " for I be very undesirous to meet with you again . " 

 " well , and I m pleased to see you re cautious , too , " say the Writer . " but I think ye take a risk to lay so considerable a sum at my discretion . " 

 he say this with a plain sneer . 

 " I ll have to run the hazard , " I reply . " o , and there s another service I would ask , and that s to direct I to a lodging , for I have no roof to my head . but it must be a lodging I may seem to have hit upon by accident , for it would never do if the Lord Advocate be to get any jealousy of our acquaintance . " 

 " Ye may set your weary spirit at rest , " say he . " I will never name your name , sir ; and it s my belief the Advocate be still so much to be sympathise with that he doesnae ken of your existence . " 

 I see I have get to the wrong side of the man . 

 " there s a braw day come for he , then , " say I , " for he ll have to learn of it on the deaf side of his head no later than to - morrow , when I call on he . " 

 " when ye call on he ! " repeat Mr. Stewart . " be I daft , or be you ! what take ye near the Advocate ! " 

 " o , just to give myself up , " say I. 

 " Mr. Balfour , " he cry , " be ye make a mock of I ? " 

 " no , sir , " say I , " though I think you have allow yourself some such freedom with myself . but I give you to understand once and for all that I be in no jesting spirit . " 

 " nor yet I , " say Stewart . " and I give yon to understand   if that s to be the word   that I like the look of your behaviour less and less . you come here to I with all sort of proposition , which will put I in a train of very doubtful act and bring I among very undesirable person this many a day to come . and then you tell I you re go straight out of my office to make your peace with the Advocate ! Alan s button here or Alan s button there , the four quarter of Alan wouldnae bribe I far in . " 

 " I would take it with a little more temper , " say I , " and perhaps we can avoid what you object to . I can see no way for it but to give myself up , but perhaps you can see another ; and if you could , I could never deny but what I would be rather relieve . for I think my traffic with his lordship be little likely to agree with my health . there s just the one thing clear , that I have to give my evidence ; for I hope it ll save Alan s character   what s left of it , and James s neck , which be the more immediate . " 

 he be silent for a breathing - space , and then , " my man , " say he , " you ll never be allow to give such evidence . " 

 " we ll have to see about that , " say I ; " I m stiff - neck when I like . " 

 " Ye muckle ass ! " cry Stewart , " it s James they want ; James have get to hang Alan , too , if they could catch he but James whatever ! go near the Advocate with any such business , and you ll see ! he ll find a way to muzzle , ye . " 

 " I think well of the Advocate than that , " say I. 

 " the Advocate be dam ! " cry he . " it s the Campbells , man ! you ll have the whole clanjamfry of they on your back ; and so will the Advocate too , poor body ! it s extraordinar ye can not see where ye stand ! if there s no fair way to stop your gab , there s a foul one gap . they can put ye in the dock , do ye no see that ? " he cry , and stab I with one finger in the leg . 

 " ay , " say I , " I be tell that same no far back than this morning by another lawyer . " 

 " and who be he ? " ask Stewart , " he speak sense at least . " 

 I tell I must be excuse from name he , for he be a decent stout old Whig , and have little mind to be mix up in such affair . 

 " I think all the world seem to be mix up in it ! " cry Stewart . " but what say you ? " 

 " I tell he what have pass between Rankeillor and myself before the house of Shaws . 

 " well , and so ye will hang ! " say he . " ye ll hang beside James Stewart . there s your fortune tell . " 

 " I hope well of it yet than that , " say I ; " but I could never deny there be a risk . " 

 " risk ! " say he , and then sit silent again . " I ought to thank you for your staunchness to my friend , to whom you show a very good spirit , " he say , " if you have the strength to stand by it . but I warn you that you re wad deep . I wouldn t put myself in your place   I that s a Stewart bear !   for all the Stewarts that ever there be since Noah . risk ? ay , I take over - many ; but to be try in court before a Campbell jury and a Campbell judge , and that in a Campbell country and upon a Campbell quarrel think what you like of I , Balfour , it s beyond I . " 

 " it s a different way of thinking , I suppose , " say I ; " I be bring up to this one by my father before I . " 

 " glory to his bone ! he have leave a decent son to his name , " say he . " yet I would not have you judge I over - sorely . my case be doom hard . see , sir , ye tell I ye re a Whig : I wonder what I be . no Whig to be sure ; I couldnae be just that . but laigh in your ear , man I m maybe no very keen on the other side . " 

 " be that a fact ? " cry I. " it s what I would think of a man of your intelligence . " 

 " Hut ! none of your whillywha ! "   4   cry he . " there s intelligence upon both side . but for my private part I have no particular desire to harm King George ; and as for King James , God bless he ! he do very well for I across the water . I m a lawyer , ye see : fond of my book and my bottle , a good plea , a well - draw deed , a crack in the Parliament House with other lawyer body , and perhaps a turn at the golf on a Saturday at e en . where do ye come in with your Hieland plaid and claymore ? " 

 " well , " say I , " it s a fact ye have little of the wild Highlandman . " 

 " little ? " quoth he . " nothing , man ! and yet I m Hieland bear , and when the clan pipe , who but I have to dance ! the clan and the name , that go by all . it s just what you say yourself ; my father learn it to I , and a bonny trade I have of it . Treason and traitor , and the smuggling of they out and in ; and the french recruiting , weary fall it ! and the smuggling through of the recruit ; and their plea a sorrow of their plea ! here have I be move one for young Ardsheil , my cousin ; claim the estate under the marriage contract a forfeit estate ! I tell they it be nonsense : muckle they care ! and there be I cock behind a yadvocate that like the business as little as myself , for it be fair ruin to the pair of we a black mark , disaffect , brand on our hurdie , like folk s name upon their kye ! and what can I do ? I m a Stewart , ye see , and must fend for my clan and family . then no later by than yesterday there be one of our Stewart lad carry to the Castle . what for ? I ken fine : Act of 1736 : recruit for King Lewie . and you ll see , he ll whistle I in to be his lawyer , and there ll be another black mark on my chara ter ! I tell you fair : if I but ken the heid of a hebrew word from the hurdie of it , be dam but I would fling the whole thing up and turn minister ! " 

 " it s rather a hard position , " say I. 

 " doom hard ! " cry he . " and that s what make I think so much of ye you that s no Stewart to stick your head so deep in Stewart business . and for what , I do not know : unless it be the sense of duty . " 

 " I hope it will be that , " say I. 

 " well , " say he , " it s a grand quality . but here be my clerk back ; and , by your leave , we ll pick a bit of dinner , all the three of we . when that s do , I ll give you the direction of a very decent man , that ll be very fain to have you for a lodger . and I ll fill your pocket to ye , forbye , out of your ain bag . for this business ll not be near as dear as ye suppose not even the ship part of it . " 

 I make he a sign that his clerk be within hearing . 

 " Hoot , ye neednae mind for Robbie , " cry he . " a Stewart , too , puir deevil ! and have smuggle out more french recruit and traffic Papists than what he have hair upon his face . why , it s Robin that manage that branch of my affair . who will we have now , Rob , for across the water ! " 

 " there ll be Andie Scougal , in the Thristle , " reply Rob . " I see Hoseason the other day , but it seem he s want the ship . then there ll be Tam Stobo ; but I m none so sure of Tam . I ve see he collogue with some gey queer acquaintance ; and if be anybody important , I would give Tam the go - by . " 

 " the head s worth two hundred pound , Robin , " say Stewart . 

 " Gosh , that ll no be Alan Breck ! " cry the clerk . 

 " just Alan , " say his master . 

 " weary wind ! that s sayrious , " cry Robin . " I ll try Andie , then ; Andie ll be the good . " 

 " it seem it s quite a big business , " I observe . 

 " Mr. Balfour , there s no end to it , " say Stewart . 

 " there be a name your clerk mention , " I go on : " Hoseason . that must be my man , I think : Hoseason , of the brig Covenant . would you set your trust on he ? " 

 " he didnae behave very well to you and Alan , " say Mr. Stewart ; " but my mind of the man in general be rather otherwise . if he have take Alan on board his ship on an agreement , it s my notion he would have prove a just dealer . how say ye , Rob ? " 

 " no more honest skipper in the trade than Eli , " say the clerk . " I would lippen to   5   Eli s word ay , if it be the Chevalier , or appin himsel , " he add . 

 " and it be he that bring the doctor , wasnae t ? " ask the master . 

 " he be the very man , " say the clerk . 

 " and I think he take the doctor back ? " say Stewart . 

 " ay , with his sporran full ! " cry Robin . " and Eli kent of that ! "   6 

 " well , it seem it s hard to ken folk rightly , " say I. 

 " that be just what I forget when ye come in , Mr. Balfour ! " say the Writer . 

 CHAPTER III I go to PILRIG 

 the next morning , I be no soon awake in my new lodging than I be up and into my new clothe ; and no soon the breakfast swallow , than I be forth on my adventurer . Alan , I could hope , be fend for ; James be like to be a more difficult affair , and I could not but think that enterprise might cost I dear , even as everybody say to whom I have open my opinion . it seem I be come to the top of the mountain only to cast myself down ; that I have clamber up , through so many and hard trial , to be rich , to be recognise , to wear city clothe and a sword to my side , all to commit mere suicide at the last end of it , and the bad kind of suicide , besides , which be to get hang at the King s charge . 

 what be I do it for ? I ask , as I go down the high Street and out north by Leith Wynd . first I say it be to save James Stewart ; and no doubt the memory of his distress , and his wife s cry , and a word or so I have let drop on that occasion work upon I strongly . at the same time I reflect that it be   or ought to be   the most indifferent matter to my father s son , whether James die in his bed or from a scaffold . he be Alan s cousin , to be sure ; but so far as regard Alan , the good thing would be to lie low , and let the king , and his Grace of Argyll , and the corbie crow , pick the bone of his kinsman their own way . nor could I forget that , while we be all in the pot together , James have show no such particular anxiety whether for Alan or I . 

 next it come upon I I be act for the sake of justice : and I think that a fine word , and reason it out that   since we dwelt in polity , at some discomfort to each one of we   the main thing of all must still be justice , and the death of any innocent man a wound upon the whole community . next , again , it be the Accuser of the Brethren that give I a turn of his argument ; bade I think shame for pretend myself concerned in these high matter , and tell I I be but a prating vain child , who have speak big word to Rankeillor and to Stewart , and hold myself bind upon my vanity to make good that boastfulness . Nay , and he hit I with the other end of the stick ; for he accuse I of a kind of artful cowardice , go about at the expense of a little risk to purchase great safety . no doubt , until I have declare and clear myself , I might any day encounter Mungo Campbell or the sheriff s officer , and be recognise , and drag into the Appin murder by the heel ; and , no doubt , in case I could manage my declaration with success , I should breathe more free for ever after . but when I look this argument full in the face I could see nothing to be ashamed of . as for the rest , " here be the two road , " I think , " and both go to the same place . it s unjust that James should hang if I can save he ; and it would be ridiculous in I to have talk so much and then do nothing . it s lucky for James of the Glens that I have boast beforehand ; and none so unlucky for myself , because now I m committed to do right . I have the name of a gentleman and the mean of one ; it would be a poor duty that I be want in the essence . " and then I think this be a Pagan spirit , and say a prayer in to myself , ask for what courage I might lack , and that I might go straight to my duty like a soldier to battle , and come off again scatheless , as so many do . 

 this train of reasoning bring I to a more resolve complexion ; though it be far from close up my sense of the danger that surround I , nor of how very apt I be   if I go on   to stumble on the ladder of the gallow . it be a plain , fair morning , but the wind in the east . the little chill of it sing in my blood , and give I a feeling of the autumn , and the dead leaf , and dead folk body in their graf . it seem the devil be in it , if I be to die in that tide of my fortune and for other folk affair . on the top of the Calton Hill , though it be not the customary time of year for that diversion , some child be cry and run with their kite . these toy appear very plain against the sky ; I remark a great one soar on the wind to a high altitude and then plump among the whin ; and I think to myself at sight of it , " there go Davie . " 

 my way lie over Mouter s Hill , and through an end of a clachan on the braeside among field . there be a whirr of loom in it go from house to house ; bee bum in the garden ; the neighbour that I see at the doorstep talk in a strange tongue ; and I find out later that this be Picardy , a village where the french weaver work for the Linen Company . here I get a fresh direction for Pilrig , my destination ; and a little beyond , on the wayside , come by a gibbet and two man hang in chain . they be dip in tar , as the manner be ; the wind span they , the chain clatter , and the bird hang about the uncanny jumping - jack and cry . the sight come on I suddenly , like an illustration of my fear , I could scarce be do with examine it and drink in discomfort . and , as I thus turn and turn about the gibbet , what should I strike on , but a weird old wife , that sit behind a leg of it , and nod , and talk aloud to herself with beck and courtesy . 

 " who be these two , mother ? " I ask , and point to the corps . 

 " a blessing on your precious face ! " she cry . " twa joe   7   o mine : just two o my old joe , my hinny dear . " 

 " what do they suffer for ? " I ask . 

 " Ou , just for the guid cause , " say she . " aften I spae to they the way that it would end . twa shillin scot : no pickle mair ; and there be twa bonny callant hingin for t ! they take it frae a wean   8   belange to Brouchton . " 

 " ay ! " say I to myself , and not to the daft limmer , " and do they come to such a figure for so poor a business ? this be to lose all indeed . " 

 " Gie s your loof ,   9   hinny , " say she , " and let I spae your weird to ye . " 

 " no , mother , " say I , " I see far enough the way I be . it s an unco thing to see too far in front . " 

 " I read it in your bree , " she say . " there s a bonnie lassie that have bricht een , and there s a wee man in a braw coat , and a big man in a pouthered wig , and there s the shadow of the wuddy ,   10   joe , that lie braid across your path . Gie s your loof , hinny , and let Auld Merren spae it to ye bonny . " 

 the two chance shot that seem to point at Alan and the daughter of James more strike I hard ; and I flee from the eldritch creature , cast she a baubee , which she continue to sit and play with under the move shadow of the hanged . 

 my way down the causeway of Leith Walk would have be more pleasant to I but for this encounter . the old rampart run among field , the like of they I have never see for artfulness of agriculture ; I be pleased , besides , to be so far in the still countryside ; but the shackle of the gibbet clatter in my head ; and the mope and mow of the old witch , and the thought of the dead man , hag - ride my spirit . to hang on a gallow , that seem a hard case ; and whether a man come to hang there for two shilling scot , or   as Mr. Stewart have it   from the sense of duty , once he be tar and shackle and hang up , the difference seem small . there might David Balfour hang , and other lad pass on their errand and think light of he ; and old daft limmer sit at a leg - foot and spae their fortune ; and the clean genty maid go by , and look to the other aide , and hold a nose . I see they plain , and they have grey eye , and their screen upon their head be of the Drummed colour . 

 I be thus in the poor of spirit , though still pretty resolve , when I come in view of Pilrig , a pleasant gable house set by the walkside among some brave young wood . the laird s horse be stand saddle at the door as I come up , but himself be in the study , where he receive I in the midst of learn work and musical instrument , for he be not only a deep philosopher but much of a musician . he greet I at first pretty well , and when he have read Rankeillor s letter , place himself obligingly at my disposal . 

 " and what be it , cousin David ! " say he " since it appear that we be cousin what be this that I can do for you ! a word to prestongrange ! doubtless that be easily give . but what should be the word ? " 

 " Mr. Balfour , " say I , " if I be to tell you my whole story the way it fall out , it s my opinion   and it be Rankeillor s before I   that you would be very little make up with it . " 

 " I be sorry to hear this of you , kinsman , " say he . 

 " I must not take that at your hand , Mr. Balfour , " say I ; " I have nothing to my charge to make I sorry , or you for I , but just the common infirmity of mankind . the guilt of Adam s first sin , the want of original righteousness , and the corruption of my whole nature , so much I must answer for , and I hope I have be teach where to look for help , " I say ; for I judge from the look of the man he would think the well of I if I know my question .   11   " but in the way of worldly honour I have no great stumble to reproach myself with ; and my difficulty have befall I very much against my will and   by all that I can see   without my fault . my trouble be to have become dip in a political complication , which it be judge you would be blythe to avoid a knowledge of . " 

 " why , very well , Mr. David , " he reply , " I be pleased to see you be all that Rankeillor represent . and for what you say of political complication , you do I no more than justice . it be my study to be beyond suspicion , and indeed outside the field of it . the question be , " say he , " how , if I be to know nothing of the matter , I can very well assist you ? " 

 " why sir , " say I , " I propose you should write to his lordship , that I be a young man of reasonable good family and of good mean : both of which I believe to be the case . " 

 " I have Rankeillor s word for it , " say Mr. Balfour , " and I count that a warran - dice against all deadly . " 

 " to which you might add   if you will take my word for so much   that I be a good churchman , loyal to King George , and so bring up , " I go on . 

 " none of which will do you any harm , " say Mr. Balfour . 

 " then you might go on to say that I seek his lordship on a matter of great moment , connect with his Majesty s service and the administration of justice , " I suggest . 

 " as I be not to hear the matter , " say the laird , " I will not take upon myself to qualify its weight . great moment therefore fall , and moment along with it . for the rest I might express myself much as you propose . " 

 " and then , sir , " say I , and rub my neck a little with my thumb , " then I would be very desirous if you could slip in a word that might perhaps tell for my protection . " 

 " protection ? " say he , " for your protection ! here be a phrase that somewhat dampen I . if the matter be so dangerous , I own I would be a little loath to move in it blindfold . " 

 " I believe I could indicate in two word where the thing stick , " say I. 

 " perhaps that would be the good , " say he . 

 " well , it s the Appin murder , " say I. 

 he hold up both his hand . " sir ! sir ! " cry he . 

 I think by the expression of his face and voice that I have lose my helper . 

 " let I explain . . . " I begin . 

 " I thank you kindly , I will hear no more of it , " say he . " I decline in toto to hear more of it . for your name s sake and Rankeillor s , and perhaps a little for your own , I will do what I can to help you ; but I will hear no more upon the fact . and it be my first clear duty to warn you . these be deep water , Mr. David , and you be a young man . be cautious and think twice . " 

 " it be to be suppose I will have think oftener than that , Mr. Balfour , " say I , " and I will direct your attention again to Rankeillor s letter , where   I hope and believe   he have register his approval of that which I design . " 

 " well , well , " say he ; and then again , " well , well ! I will do what I can for you . " there with he take a pen and paper , sit a while in thought , and begin to write with much consideration . " I understand that Rankeillor approve of what you have in mind ? " he ask presently . 

 " after some discussion , sir , he bid I to go forward in God s name , " say I. 

 " that be the name to go in , " say Mr. Balfour , and resume his writing . presently , he sign , re - read what he have write , and address I again . " now here , Mr. David , " say he , " be a letter of introduction , which I will seal without closing , and give into your hand open , as the form require . but , since I be act in the dark , I will just read it to you , so that you may see if it will secure your end 

 " Pilrig , August 26th , 1751 . 

 " my Lord , this be to bring to your notice my namesake and cousin , David Balfour Esquire of Shaws , a young gentleman of unblemished descent and good estate . he have enjoy , besides , the more valuable advantage of a godly training , and his political principle be all that your lordship can desire . I be not in Mr. Balfour s confidence , but I understand he to have a matter to declare , touch his Majesty s service and the administration of justice ; purpose for which your Lordship s zeal be know . I should add that the young gentleman s intention be know to and approve by some of his friend , who will watch with hopeful anxiety the event of his success or failure . 

 " Whereupon , " continue Mr. Balfour , " I have subscribe myself with the usual compliment . you observe I have say some of your friend ; I hope you can justify my plural ? " 

 " perfectly , sir ; my purpose be know and approve by more than one , " say I. " and your letter , which I take a pleasure to thank you for , be all I could have hop . " 

 " it be all I could squeeze out , " say he ; " and from what I know of the matter you design to meddle in , I can only pray God that it may prove sufficient . " 

 CHAPTER IV LORD ADVOCATE PRESTONGRANGE 

 my kinsman keep I to a meal , " for the honour of the roof , " he say ; and I believe I make the well speed on my return . I have no thought but to be do with the next stage , and have myself fully commit ; to a person circumstance as I be , the appearance of close a door on hesitation and temptation be itself extremely tempting ; and I be the more disappointed , when I come to Prestongrange s house , to be inform he be abroad . I believe it be true at the moment , and for some hour after ; and then I have no doubt the Advocate come home again , and enjoy himself in a neighbouring chamber among friend , while perhaps the very fact of my arrival be forget . I would have go away a dozen time , only for this strong drawing to have do with my declaration out of hand and be able to lay I down to sleep with a free conscience . at first I read , for the little cabinet where I be leave contain a variety of book . but I fear I read with little profit ; and the weather fall cloudy , the dusk come up early than usual , and my cabinet be light with but a loophole of a window , I be at last oblige to desist from this diversion   such as it be , and pass the rest of my time of wait in a very burthensome vacuity . the sound of people talk in a near chamber , the pleasant note of a harpsichord , and once the voice of a lady singing , bear I a kind of company . 

 I do not know the hour , but the darkness be long come , when the door of the cabinet open , and I be aware , by the light behind he , of a tall figure of a man upon the threshold . I rise at once . 

 " be anybody there ? " he ask . " who in that ? " 

 " I be bearer of a letter from the laird of Pilrig to the Lord Advocate , " say I. 

 " have you be here long ? " he ask . 

 " I would not like to hazard an estimate of how many hour , " say I. 

 " it be the first I hear of it , " he reply , with a chuckle . " the lad must have forget you . but you be in the bit at last , for I be Prestongrange . " 

 so say , he pass before I into the next room , whither   upon his sign   I follow he , and where he light a candle and take his place before a business - table . it be a long room , of a good proportion , wholly line with book . that small spark of light in a corner strike out the man s handsome person and strong face . he be flushed , his eye water and sparkle , and before he sit down I observe he to sway back and forth . no doubt , he have be sup liberally ; but his mind and tongue be under full control . 

 " well , sir , sit ye down , " say he , " and let we see Pilrig s letter . " 

 he glance it through in the beginning carelessly , look up and bow when he come to my name ; but at the last word I think I observe his attention to redouble , and I make sure he read they twice . all this while you be to suppose my heart be beat , for I have now cross my Rubicon and be come fairly on the field of battle . 

 " I be pleased to make your acquaintance , Mr. Balfour , " he say , when he have do . " let I offer you a glass of claret . " 

 " under your favour , my lord , I think it would scarce be fair on I , " say I. " I have come here , as the letter will have mention , on a business of some gravity to myself ; and , as I be little use with wine , I might be the soon affected . " 

 " you shall be the judge , " say he . " but if you will permit , I believe I will even have the bottle in myself . " 

 he touch a bell , and a footman come , as at a signal , bring wine and glass . 

 " you be sure you will not join I ? " ask the Advocate . " well , here be to our well acquaintance ! in what way can I serve you ? " 

 " I should , perhaps , begin by tell you , my lord , that I be here at your own press invitation , " say I. 

 " you have the advantage of I somewhere , " say he , " for I profess I think I never hear of you before this evening . " 

 " right , my lord ; the name be , indeed , new to you , " say I. " and yet you have be for some time extremely wishful to make my acquaintance , and have declare the same in public . " 

 " I wish you would afford I a clue , " say he . " I be no Daniel . " 

 " it will perhaps serve for such , " say I , " that if I be in a jest humour which be far from the case I believe I might lay a claim on your lordship for two hundred pound . " 

 " in what sense ? " he inquire . 

 " in the sense of reward offer for my person , " say I. 

 he thrust away his glass once and for all , and sit straight up in the chair where he have be previously lolling . " what be I to understand ? " say he . 

 " a tall strong lad of about eighteen , " I quote , " speak like a Lowlander and have no beard . " 

 " I recognise those word , " say he , " which , if you have come here with any ill - judge intention of amuse yourself , be like to prove extremely prejudicial to your safety . " 

 " my purpose in this , " I reply , " be just entirely as serious as life and death , and you have understand I perfectly . I be the boy who be speak with Glenure when he be shoot . " 

 " I can only suppose   see you here   that you claim to be innocent , " say he . 

 " the inference be clear , " I say . " I be a very loyal subject to King George , but if I have anything to reproach myself with , I would have have more discretion than to walk into your den . " 

 " I be glad of that , " say he . " this horrid crime , Mr. Balfour , be of a dye which can not permit any clemency . blood have be barbarously shed . it have be shed in direct opposition to his Majesty and our whole frame of law , by those who be their known and public oppugnant . I take a very high sense of this . I will not deny that I consider the crime as directly personal to his Majesty . " 

 " and unfortunately , my lord , " I add , a little drily , " directly personal to another great personage who may be nameless . " 

 " if you mean anything by those word , I must tell you I consider they unfit for a good subject ; and be they speak publicly I should make it my business to take note of they , " say he . " you do not appear to I to recognise the gravity of your situation , or you would be more careful not to pejorate the same by word which glance upon the purity of justice . Justice , in this country , and in my poor hand , be no respecter of person . " 

 " you give I too great a share in my own speech , my lord , " say I. " I do but repeat the common talk of the country , which I have hear everywhere , and from man of all opinion as I come along . " 

 " when you be come to more discretion you will understand such talk in not to be listen to , how much less repeat , " say the Advocate . " but I acquit you of an ill intention . that nobleman , whom we all honour , and who have indeed be wound in a near place by the late barbarity , sit too high to be reach by these aspersion . the Duke of Argyle you see that I deal plainly with you take it to heart as I do , and as we be both bind to do by our judicial function and the service of his Majesty ; and I could wish that all hand , in this ill age , be equally clean of family rancour . but from the accident that this be a Campbell who have fall martyr to his duty as who else but the Campbells have ever put themselves foremost on that path ? I may say it , who be no Campbell and that the chief of that great house happen   for all our advantage   to be the present head of the College of Justice , small mind and disaffect tongue be set agog in every changehouse in the country ; and I find a young gentleman like Mr. Balfour so ill - advise as to make himself their echo . " so much he speak with a very oratorical delivery , as if in court , and then decline again upon the manner of a gentleman . " all this apart , " say he . " it now remain that I should learn what I be to do with you . " 

 " I have think it be rather I that should learn the same from your lordship , " say I. 

 " ay , true , " say the Advocate . " but , you see , you come to I well recommend . there be a good honest Whig name to this letter , " say he , pick it up a moment from the table . " and extra - judicially , Mr. Balfour there be always the possibility of some arrangement , I tell you , and I tell you beforehand that you may be the more upon your guard , your fate lie with I singly . in such a matter   be it say with reverence   I be more powerful than the King s Majesty ; and should you please I and of course satisfy my conscience in what remain to be hold of our interview , I tell you it may remain between ourselves . " 

 " mean how ? " I ask . 

 " why , I mean it thus , Mr. Balfour , " say he , " that if you give satisfaction , no soul need know so much as that you visit my house ; and you may observe that I do not even call my clerk . " 

 I see what way he be drive . " I suppose it be needless anyone should be inform upon my visit , " say I , " though the precise nature of my gain by that I can not see . I be not at all ashamed of come here . " 

 " and have no cause to be , " say he , encouragingly . " nor yet   if you be careful   to fear the consequence . " 

 " my lord , " say I , " speak under your correction , I be not very easy to be frightened . " 

 " and I be sure I do not seek to frighten you , " say he . " but to the interrogation ; and let I warn you to volunteer nothing beyond the question I shall ask you . it may consist very immediately with your safety . I have a great discretion , it be true , but there be bound to it . " 

 " I shall try to follow your lordship s advice , " say I. 

 he spread a sheet of paper on the table and write a heading . " it appear you be present , by the way , in the wood of Lettermore at the moment of the fatal shot , " he begin . " be this by accident ? " 

 " by accident , " say I. 

 " how come you in speech with Colin Campbell ? " he ask . 

 " I be inquire my way of he to aucharn , " I reply . 

 I observe he do not write this answer down . 

 " H m , true , " say he , " I have forget that . and do you know , Mr. Balfour , I would dwell , if I be you , as little as might be on your relation with these Stewarts . it might be find to complicate our business . I be not yet inclined to regard these matter as essential . " 

 " I have think , my lord , that all point of fact be equally material in such a case , " say I. 

 " you forget we be now try these Stewarts , " he reply , with great significance . " if we should ever come to be try you , it will be very different ; and I shall press these very question that I be now willing to glide upon . but to resume : I have it here in Mr. Mungo Campbell s precognition that you run immediately up the brae . how come that ? " 

 " not immediately , my lord , and the cause be my seeing of the murderer . " 

 " you see he , then ? " 

 " as plain as I see your lordship , though not so near hand . " 

 " you know he ? " 

 " I should know he again . " 

 " in your pursuit you be not so fortunate , then , as to overtake he ? " 

 " I be not . " 

 " be he alone ? " 

 " he be alone . " 

 " there be no one else in that neighbourhood ? " 

 " Alan Breck Stewart be not far off , in a piece of a wood . " 

 the Advocate lay his pen down . " I think we be play at cross purpose , " say he , " which you will find to prove a very ill amusement for yourself . " 

 " I content myself with follow your lordship s advice , and answer what I be ask , " say I. 

 " be so wise as to bethink yourself in time , " say he , " I use you with the most anxious tenderness , which you scarce seem to appreciate , and which   unless you be more careful   may prove to be in vain . " 

 " I do appreciate your tenderness , but conceive it to be mistake , " I reply , with something of a falter , for I see we be come to grip at last . " I be here to lay before you certain information , by which I shall convince you Alan have no hand whatever in the killing of Glenure . " 

 the Advocate appear for a moment at a stick , sit with pursed lip , and blink his eye upon I like an angry cat . " Mr. Balfour , " he say at last , " I tell you pointedly you go an ill way for your own interest . " 

 " my lord , " I say , " I be as free of the charge of consider my own interest in this matter as your lordship . as God judge I , I have but the one design , and that be to see justice execute and the innocent go clear . if in pursuit of that I come to fall under your lordship s displeasure , I must bear it as I may . " 

 at this he rise from his chair , light a second candle , and for a while gaze upon I steadily . I be surprised to see a great change of gravity fall upon his face , and I could have almost think he be a little pale . 

 " you be either very simple , or extremely the reverse , and I see that I must deal with you more confidentially , " say he . " this be a political case ah , yes , Mr. Balfour ! whether we like it or no , the case be political and I tremble when I think what issue may depend from it . to a political case , I need scarce tell a young man of your education , we approach with very different thought from one which be criminal only . salus populi suprema lex be a maxim susceptible of great abuse , but it have that force which we find elsewhere only in the law of nature : I mean it have the force of necessity .  CHAPTER VI UMQUILE the MASTER of LOVAT

 " I be afraid you do not like my name , sir , " say I , annoy with myself to be annoy with such a rustical fellow . 

 " no , " say he , " but I wass thinking . " 

 " I would not advise you to make a practice of that , sir , " say I. " I feel sure you would not find it to agree with you . " 

 " Tit you effer hear where Alan Grigor fand the tang ? " say he . 

 I ask he what he could possibly mean , and he answer , with a heckle laugh , that he think I must have find the poker in the same place and swallow it . 

 there could be no mistake about this , and my cheek burn . 

 " before I go about to put affront on gentleman , " say I , " I think I would learn the english language first . " 

 he take I by the sleeve with a nod and a wink and lead I quietly outside Hope Park . but no soon be we beyond the view of the promenader , than the fashion of his countenance change . " you tam lowland scoon rel ! " cry he , and hit I a buffet on the jaw with his closed fist . 

 I pay he as good or well on the return ; whereupon he step a little back and take off his hat to I decorously . 

 " enough plow I think , " say he . " I will be the offended shentleman , for who effer hear of such suffeeciency as tell a shentleman that be the king s officer he cannae speak Cot s English ? we have sword at our hurdle , and here be the King s Park at hand . will ye walk first , or let I show ye the way ? " 

 I return his bow , tell he to go first , and follow he . as he go I hear he grumble to himself about Cot s English and the King s coat , so that I might have suppose he to be seriously offend . but his manner at the beginning of our interview be there to belie he . it be manifest he have come prepared to fasten a quarrel on I , right or wrong ; manifest that I be take in a fresh contrivance of my enemy ; and to I   conscious as I be of my deficiency   manifest enough that I should be the one to fall in our encounter . 

 as we come into that rough rocky desert of the King s Park I be tempt half - a - dozen time to take to my heel and run for it , so loath be I to show my ignorance in fencing , and so much averse to die or even to be wound . but I consider if their malice go as far as this , it would likely stick at nothing ; and that to fall by the sword , however ungracefully , be still an improvement on the gallow . I consider besides that by the unguarded pertness of my word and the quickness of my blow I have put myself quite out of court ; and that even if I run , my adversary would probably pursue and catch I , which would add disgrace to my misfortune . so that , take all in all , I continue march behind he , much as a man follow the hangman , and certainly with no more hope . 

 we go about the end of the long craig , and come into the Hunter s bog . here , on a piece of fair turf , my adversary draw . there be nobody there to see we but some bird ; and no resource for I but to follow his example , and stand on guard with the good face I could display . it seem it be not good enough for Mr. Dancansby , who spy some flaw in my manouvre , pause , look upon I sharply , and come off and on , and menace I with his blade in the air . as I have see no such proceeding from Alan , and be besides a good deal affect with the proximity of death , I grow quite bewilder , stand helpless , and could have long to run away . 

 " fat deil ail she ? " cry the lieutenant . 

 and suddenly engage , he twitch the sword out of my grasp and send it fly far among the rush . 

 Twice be this manouvre repeat ; and the third time when I bring back my humiliated weapon , I find he have return his own to the scabbard , and stand await I with a face of some anger , and his hand clasp under his skirt . 

 " Pe tamne if I touch you ! " he cry , and ask I bitterly what right I have to stand up before " shentleman " when I do not know the back of a sword from the front of it . 

 I answer that be the fault of my upbringing ; and would he do I the justice to say I have give he all the satisfaction it be unfortunately in my power to offer , and have stand up like a man ? 

 " and that be the truth , " say he . " I be fery prave myself , and pold as a lion . but to stand up there and you ken naethe of fence ! the way that you do , I declare it be peyond I . and I be sorry for the plow ; though I declare I pelief your own be the eld brother , and my heid still sing with it . and I declare if I have ken what way it wass , I would not put a hand to such a piece of pusiness . " 

 " that be handsomely say , " I reply , " and I be sure you will not stand up a second time to be the actor for my private enemy . " 

 " indeed , no , Palfour , " say he ; " and I think I be use extremely suffeeciently myself to be set up to fecht with an auld wife , or all the same as a bairn whateffer ! and I will tell the Master so , and fecht he , by Cot , himself ! " 

 " and if you know the nature of Mr. Simon s quarrel with I , " say I , " you would be yet the more affronted to be mingle up with such affair . " 

 he swear he could well believe it ; that all the Lovats be make of the same meal and the devil be the miller that grind that ; then suddenly shake I by the hand , he vow I be a pretty enough fellow after all , that it be a thousand pity I have be neglect , and that if he could find the time , he would give an eye himself to have I educate . 

 " you can do I a well service than even what you propose , " say I ; and when he have ask its nature " come with I to the house of one of my enemy , and testify how I have carry myself this day , " I tell he . " that will be the true service . for though he have send I a gallant adversary for the first , the thought in Mr. Simon s mind be merely murder . there will be a second and then a third ; and by what you have see of my cleverness with the cold steel , you can judge for yourself what be like to be the upshot . " 

 " and I would not like it myself , if I be no more of a man than what you wass ! " he cry . " but I will do you right , Palfour . lead on ! " 

 if I have walk slowly on the way into that accurse park my heel be light enough on the way out . they keep time to a very good old air , that be as ancient as the Bible , and the word of it be : " surely the bitterness of death be pass . " I mind that I be extremely thirsty , and have a drink at Saint Margaret s well on the road down , and the sweetness of that water pass belief . we go through the sanctuary , up the Canongate , in by the Netherbow , and straight to Prestongrange s door , talk as we come and arrange the detail of our affair . the footman own his master be at home , but declare he engage with other gentleman on very private business , and his door forbid . 

 " my business be but for three minute , and it can not wait , " say I. " you may say it be by no means private , and I shall be even glad to have some witness . " 

 as the man depart unwillingly enough upon this errand , we make so bold as to follow he to the ante - chamber , whence I could hear for a while the murmuring of several voice in the room within . the truth be , they be three at the one table Prestongrange , Simon Fraser , and Mr. Erskine , Sheriff of Perth ; and as they be meet in consultation on the very business of the Appin murder , they be a little disturbed at my appearance , but decide to receive I . 

 " well , well , Mr. Balfour , and what bring you here again ? and who be this you bring with you ? " say Prestongrange . 

 as for Fraser , he look before he on the table . 

 " he be here to bear a little testimony in my favour , my lord , which I think it very needful you should hear , " say I , and turn to Duncansby . 

 " I have only to say this , " say the lieutenant , " that I stand up this day with Palfour in the Hunter s Pog , which I be now fery sorry for , and he behave himself as pretty as a shentleman could ask it . and I have creat respect for palfour , " he add . 

 " I thank you for your honest expression , " say I. 

 Whereupon Duncansby make his bow to the company , and leave the chamber , as we have agree upon before . 

 " what have I to do with this ? " say Prestongrange . 

 " I will tell your lordship in two word , " say I. " I have bring this gentleman , a King s officer , to do I so much justice . now I think my character be cover , and until a certain date , which your lordship can very well supply , it will be quite in vain to despatch against I any more officer . I will not consent to fight my way through the garrison of the castle . " 

 the vein swell on Prestongrange s brow , and he regard I with fury . 

 " I think the devil uncouple this dog of a lad between my leg ! " he cry ; and then , turn fiercely on his neighbour , " this be some of your work , Simon , " he say . " I spy your hand in the business , and , let I tell you , I resent it . it be disloyal , when we be agree upon one expedient , to follow another in the dark . you be disloyal to I . what ! you let I send this lad to the place with my very daughter ! and because I let drop a word to you ..... fy , sir , keep your dishonour to yourself ! " 

 Simon be deadly pale . " I will be a kick - ball between you and the Duke no long , " he exclaim . " either come to an agreement , or come to a differ , and have it out among yourself . but I will no long fetch and carry , and get your contrary instruction , and be blame by both . for if I be to tell you what I think of all your Hanover business it would make your head sing . " 

 but Sheriff Erskine have preserve his temper , and now intervene smoothly . " and in the meantime , " say he , " I think we should tell Mr. Balfour that his character for valour be quite establish . he may sleep in peace . until the date he be so good as to refer to it shall be put to the proof no more . " 

 his coolness bring the other to their prudence ; and they make haste , with a somewhat distracted civility , to pack I from the house . 

 CHAPTER IX the heather ON FIRE 

 when I leave Prestongrange that afternoon I be for the first time angry . the Advocate have make a mock of I . he have pretend my testimony be to be receive and myself respect ; and in that very hour , not only be Simon practise against my life by the hand of the Highland soldier , but   as appear from his own language   Prestongrange himself have some design in operation . I count my enemy ; prestongrange with all the King s authority behind he ; and the Duke with the power of the West Highlands ; and the Lovat interest by their side to help they with so great a force in the north , and the whole clan of old Jacobite spy and trafficker . and when I remember James More , and the red head of Neil the son of Duncan , I think there be perhaps a fourth in the confederacy , and what remain of Rob Roy s old desperate sept of caterans would be band against I with the other . one thing be requisite some strong friend or wise adviser . the country must be full of such , both able and eager to support I , or Lovat and the Duke and Prestongrange have not be nose for expedient ; and it make I rage to think that I might brush against my champion in the street and be no wiser . 

 and just then   like an answer   a gentleman brush against I go by , give I a meaning look , and turn into a close .  " we ll have to sit upon the floor , " say he ; " but we re safe here for the time being , and I ve be weary to see ye , Mr. Balfour . "

 " Hout awa ! " cry Stewart . " I ll never believe that . "

" 

 " and how be they to bring in Alan till they can catch he ? " say I. 

 " ah , but there be a way to evite that arrestment , " say he . " sound law , too . it would be a bonny thing if , by the escape of one ill - doer another be to go scatheless , and the remeid be to summon the principal and put he to outlawry for the non - compearance . now there s four place where a person can be summon : at his dwelling - house ; at a place where he have reside forty day ; at the head burgh of the shire where he ordinarily resort ; or lastly   if there be ground to think he forth of Scotland   at the cross of Edinburgh , and the pier and shore of Leith , for sixty day . the purpose of which last provision be evident upon its face : be that outgoing ship may have time to carry news of the transaction , and the summonsing be something other than a form . now take the case of Alan . he have no dwelling - house that ever I could hear of ; I would be oblige if anyone would show I where he have live forty day together since the 45 ; there be no shire where he resort whether ordinarily or extraordinarily ; if he have a domicile at all , which I misdoubt , it must be with his regiment in France ; and if he be not yet forth of Scotland   as we happen to know and they happen to guess   it must be evident to the most dull it s what he s aim for . where , then , and what way should he be summon ? I ask it at yourself , a layman . " 

 " you have give the very word , " say I. " here at the cross , and at the pier and shore of Leith , for sixty day . " 

 " ye re a sounder Scots lawyer than Prestongrange , then ! " cry the Writer . " he have have Alan summon once ; that be on the twenty - fifth , the day that we first meet . once , and do with it . and where ? where , but at the cross of Inverary , the head burgh of the Campbells ? a word in your ear , Mr. Balfour they re not seek Alan . " 

 " what do you mean ? " I cry . " not seek he ? " 

 " by the good that I can make of it , " say he . " not want to find he , in my poor thought . they think perhaps he might set up a fair defence , upon the back of which James , the man they re really after , might climb out . this be not a case , ye see , it s a conspiracy . " 

 " yet I can tell you Prestongrange ask after Alan keenly , " say I ; " though , when I come to think of it , he be something of the easy put by . "

I may be right or wrong , that s guesswork at the good , and let I get to my fact again . it come to my ear that James and the witness the witness , Mr. Balfour ! lie in close dungeon , and shackle forbye , in the military prison at Fort William ; none allow in to they , nor they to write . the witness , Mr. Balfour ; hear ye ever the match of that ? I assure ye , no old , crooked Stewart of the gang ever out - face the law more impudently . it s clean in the two eye of the Act of Parliament of 1700 , anent wrongous imprisonment . no soon do I get the news than I petition the Lord Justice Clerk . I have his word to - day . there s law for ye ! here s justice ! " 

 he put a paper in my hand , that same mealy - mouthed , false - faced paper that be print since in the pamphlet " by a bystander , " for behoof   as the title say   of James s " poor widow and five child . "

I would have to make the journey back again betwixt here and Fort William . then would follow a fresh delay till I get fresh authority , and they have disavow the officer military man , notoriously ignorant of the law , and that I ken the ca not of it . then the journey a third time ; and there we should be on the immediate heel of the trial before I have receive my first instruction . be I not right to call this a conspiracy ? "

" they have the right to hold James in prison , yet they can not deny I to visit he . they have no right to hold the witness ; but be I to get a sight of they , that should be as free as the Lord Justice Clerk himself ! see read : for the rest , refuse to give any order to keeper of prison who be not accuse as have do anything contrary to the duty of their office . anything contrary ! sir ! and the Act of seventeen hunner ? Mr. Balfour , this make my heart to burst ; the heather be on fire inside my wame . " 

 " and the plain English of that phrase , " say I , " be that the witness be still to lie in prison and you be not to see they ? " 

 " and I be not to see they until Inverary , when the court be set ! " cry he , " and then to hear Prestongrange upon the anxious responsibility of his office and the great facility afford the defence ! but I ll begowk they there , Mr. David . I have a plan to waylay the witness upon the road , and see if I cannae get I a little harle of justice out of the military man notoriously ignorant of the law that shall command the party . " 

 it be actually so it be actually on the wayside near Tynedrum , and by the connivance of a soldier officer , that Mr. Stewart first see the witness upon the case . 

 " there be nothing that would surprise I in this business , " I remark . 

 " I ll surprise you ere I m do ! " cry he . " do ye see this ? " produce a print still wet from the press . " this be the libel : see , there s Prestongrange s name to the list of witness , and I find no word of any Balfour . but here be not the question . who do ye think pay for the printing of this paper ? "
