 " but it happen it be I ! " he cry . " not but it be print by and for themselves , for the Grants and the Erskines , and yon thief of the black midnight , Simon Fraser . but could I win to get a copy ! no ! I be to go blindfold to my defence ; I be to hear the charge for the first time in court alongst the jury . " 

 " be not this against the law ? " I ask . 

 " I can not say so much , " he reply . " it be a favour so natural and so constantly render   till this nonesuch business   that the law have never look to it . and now admire the hand of Providence ! a stranger be in Fleming s printing house , spy a proof on the floor , pick it up , and carry it to I . of all thing , it be just this libel . whereupon I have it set again print at the expense of the defence : sumptibus moesti rei ; hear ever man the like of it ? and here it be for anybody , the muckle secret out all may see it now . but how do you think I would enjoy this , that have the life of my kinsman on my conscience ? " 

 " Troth , I think you would enjoy it ill , " say I. 

 " and now you see how it be , " he conclude , " and why , when you tell I your evidence be to be let in , I laugh aloud in your face . " 

 it be now my turn . I lay before he in brief Mr. Simon s threat and offer , and the whole incident of the bravo , with the subsequent scene at Prestongrange s. of my first talk , accord to promise , I say nothing , nor indeed be it necessary . all the time I be talk Stewart nod his head like a mechanical figure ; and no soon have my voice cease , than he open his mouth and give I his opinion in two word , dwell strong on both of they . 

 " disappear yourself , " say he . 

 " I do not take you , " say I. 

 " then I ll carry you there , " say he . " by my view of it you re to disappear whatever . o , that s outside debate . the Advocate , who be not without some spunk of a remainder decency , have wring your life - safe out of Simon and the Duke . he have refuse to put you on your trial , and refuse to have you kill ; and there be the clue to their ill word together , for Simon and the Duke can keep faith with neither friend nor enemy . ye re not to be try then , and ye re not to be murder ; but I m in bitter error if ye re not to be kidnap and carry away like the Lady Grange . bet I what ye please there be their expedient ! " 

 " you make I think , " say I , and tell he of the whistle and the red - head retainer , Neil . 

 " wherever James More be there s one big rogue , never be deceive on that , " say he . " his father be none so ill a man , though a kenning on the wrong side of the law , and no friend to my family , that I should waste my breath to be defend he ! but as for James he s a brock and a blagyard . I like the appearance of this red - headed Neil as little as yourself . it look uncanny : fiegh ! it smell bad . it be old Lovat that manage the Lady Grange affair ; if young Lovat be to handle your , it ll be all in the family . what s James More in prison for ? the same offence : abduction . his man have have practice in the business . he ll be to lend they to be Simon s instrument ; and the next thing we ll be hear , James will have make his peace , or else he ll have escape ; and you ll be in Benbecula or Applecross .  " and what I want , " he resume , " be that you should disappear yourself ere they can get their hand upon ye . lie quiet until just before the trial , and spring upon they at the last of it when they ll be look for you least . this be always suppose Mr. Balfour , that your evidence be worth so very great a measure of both risk and fash . " 

 " I will tell you one thing , " say I. " I see the murderer and it be not Alan . " 

 " then , by God , my cousin s save ! " cry Stewart . " you have his life upon your tongue ; and there s neither time , risk , nor money to be spar to bring you to the trial . " he empty his pocket on the floor . "

 " and I wish that I could tell ye ! " say he , " but all the place that I could send ye to , would be just the place they would seek . no , ye must fend for yourself , and God be your guiding ! five day before the trial , September the sixteen , get word to I at the King s arm in Stirling ; and if ye ve manage for yourself as long as that , I ll see that ye reach Inverary . " 

 " one thing more , " say i. " can I no see Alan ? " 

 he seem boggle . " Hech , I would rather you wouldnae , " say he . " 

 CHAPTER X the RED - HEADED MAN 

 it be about half - past three when I come forth on the Lang Dykes . Dean be where I want to go . since Catriona dwell there , and her kinsfolk the Glengyle Macgregors appear almost certainly to be employ against I , it be just one of the few place I should have keep away from ; and be a very young man , and begin to be very much in love , I turn my face in that direction without pause . as a slave to my conscience and common sense , however , I take a measure of precaution . come over the crown of a bit of a rise in the road , I clap down suddenly among the barley and lie wait . after a while , a man go by that look to be a Highlandman , but I have never see he till that hour . presently after come Neil of the red head . the next to go past be a miller s cart , and after that nothing but manifest country people . here be enough to have turn the most foolhardy from his purpose , but my inclination run too strong the other way . I argue it out that if Neil be on that road , it be the right road to find he in , lead direct to his chief s daughter ; as for the other Highlandman , if I be to be startle off by every Highlandman I see , I would scarce reach anywhere . and have quite satisfied myself with this disingenuous debate , I make the well speed of it , and come a little after four to Mrs. Drumond - Ogilvy s. 

 both lady be within the house ; and upon my perceive they together by the open door , I pluck off my hat and say , " here be a lad come seek saxpence , " which I think might please the dowager . 

 Catriona run out to greet I heartily , and , to my surprise , the old lady seem scarce less forward than herself . I learn long afterwards that she have despatch a horseman by daylight to Rankeillor at the Queensferry , whom she know to be the doer for Shaws , and have then in her pocket a letter from that good friend of mine , present , in the most favourable view , my character and prospect . but have I read it I could scarce have see more clear in her design . maybe I be countryfeed ; at least , I be not so much so as she think ; and it be even to my homespun wit , that she be bent to hammer up a match between her cousin and a beardless boy that be something of a laird in Lothian . 

 " Saxpence have well take his broth with we , Catrine , " say she . " run and tell the lass . " 

 and for the little while we be alone be at a good deal of pain to flatter I ; always cleverly , always with the appearance of a banter , still call I Saxpence , but with such a turn that should rather uplift I in my own opinion . when Catriona return , the design become if possible more obvious ; and she show off the girl s advantage like a horse - couper with a horse . my face flame that she should think I so obtuse . now I would fancy the girl be be innocently make a show of , and then I could have beat the old carline wife with a cudgel ; and now , that perhaps these two have set their head together to entrap I , and at that I sit and gloome betwixt they like the very image of ill - will . at last the matchmaker have a well device , which be to leave the pair of we alone . when my suspicion be anyway rouse it be sometimes a little the wrong side of easy to allay they . but though I know what breed she be of , and that be a breed of thief , I could never look in Catriona s face and disbelieve she . 

 " I must not ask ? " say she , eagerly , the same moment we be leave alone . 

 " ah , but to - day I can talk with a free conscience , " I reply . " I be lightened of my pledge , and indeed   after what have come and go since morning   I would not have renew it be it ask . " 

 " tell I , " she say . " my cousin will not be so long . " 

 so I tell she the tale of the lieutenant from the first step to the last of it , make it as mirthful as I could , and , indeed , there be matter of mirth in that absurdity . 

 " and I think you will be as little fit for the ruda man as for the pretty lady , after all ! " say she , when I have do . " but what be your father that he could not learn you to draw the sword ! it be most ungentle ; I have not hear the match of that in anyone . " 

 " it be most misconvenient at least , " say I ; " and I think my father   honest man !   must have be wool - gathering to learn I Latin in the place of it . but you see I do the good I can , and just stand up like Lot s wife and let they hammer at I . " 

 " do you know what make I smile ? " say she . " well , it be this . I be make this way , that I should have be a man child . in my own thought it be so I be always ; and I go on tell myself about this thing that be to befall and that . then it come to the place of the fighting , and it come over I that I be only a girl at all event , and can not hold a sword or give one good blow ; and then I have to twist my story round about , so that the fighting be to stop , and yet I have the good of it , just like you and the lieutenant ; and I be the boy that make the fine speech all through , like Mr. David Balfour . " 

 " you be a bloodthirsty maid , " say I. 

 " well , I know it be good to sew and spin , and to make sampler , " she say , " but if you be to do nothing else in the great world , I think you will say yourself it be a driech business ; and it be not that I want to kill , I think . do ever you kill anyone ? " 

 " that I have , as it chance . two , no less , and I still a lad that should be at the college , " say I. " but yet , in the look - back , I take no shame for it . " 

 " but how do you feel , then after it ? " she ask . 

  " Deed , I sit down and grat like a bairn , " say I. 

 " I know that , too , " she cry . " I feel where these tear should come from . and at any rate , I would not wish to kill , only to be Catherine Douglas that put her arm through the staple of the bolt , where it be break . that be my chief hero . would you not love to die so for your king ? " she ask . 

 " Troth , " say I , " my affection for my king , God bless the puggy face of he , be under more control ; and I think I see death so near to I this day already , that I be rather take up with the notion of living . " 

 " right , " she say , " the right mind of a man ! only you must learn arm ; I would not like to have a friend that can not strike . but it will not have be with the sword that you kill these two ? " 

 " indeed , no , " say I , " but with a pair of pistol . and a fortunate thing it be the man be so near - hand to I , for I be about as clever with the pistol as I be with the sword . " 

 so then she draw from I the story of our battle in the brig , which I have omit in my first account of my affair . 

 " yes , " say she , " you be brave . and your friend , I admire and love he . " 

 " well , and I think anyone would ! " say I. " he have his fault like other folk ; but he be brave and staunch and kind , God bless he ! that will be a strange day when I forget Alan . " and the thought of he , and that it be within my choice to speak with he that night , have almost overcome I . 

 " and where will my head be go that I have not tell my news ! " she cry , and speak of a letter from her father , bear that she might visit he to - morrow in the castle whither he be now transfer , and that his affair be mend . " you do not like to hear it , " say she . " will you judge my father and not know he ? " 

 " I be a thousand mile from judge , " I reply . " and I give you my word I do rejoice to know your heart be lightened . if my face fall at all , as I suppose it must , you will allow this be rather an ill day for composition , and the people in power extremely ill person to be compound with . I have Simon Fraser extremely heavy on my stomach still . " 

 " ah ! " she cry , " you will not be evening these two ; and you should bear in mind that Prestongrange and James More , my father , be of the one blood . " 

 " I never hear tell of that , " say I. 

 " it be rather singular how little you be acquaint with , " say she . " one part may call themselves Grant , and one Macgregor , but they be still of the same clan . they be all the son of Alpin , from whom , I think , our country have its name . " 

 " what country be that ? " I ask . 

 " my country and your , " say she . 

 " this be my day for discover I think , " say I , " for I always think the name of it be Scotland . " 

 " Scotland be the name of what you call Ireland , " she reply . " but the old ancient true name of this place that we have our foot - sol on , and that our bone be make of , will be Alban . it be Alban they call it when our forefather will be fight for it against Rome and Alexander ; and it be call so still in your own tongue that you forget . " 

 " Troth , " say I , " and that I never learn ! " for I lack heart to take she up about the Macedonian . 

 " but your father and mother talk it , one generation with another , " say she . " and it be sing about the cradle before you or I be ever dream of ; and your name remember it still . ah , if you could talk that language you would find I another girl . the heart speak in that tongue . " 

 I have a meal with the two lady , all very good , serve in fine old plate , and the wine excellent , for it seem that Mrs. Ogilvy be rich . our talk , too , be pleasant enough ; but as soon as I see the sun decline sharply and the shadow to run out long , I rise to take my leave . for my mind be now make up to say farewell to Alan ; and it be needful I should see the tryste wood , and reconnoitre it , by daylight . Catriona come with I as far as to the garden gate . 

 " it be long till I see you now ? " she ask . 

 " it be beyond my judging , " I reply . " it will be long , it may be never . " 

 " it may be so , " say she . " and you be sorry ? " 

 I bow my head , look upon she . 

 " so be I , at all event , " say she . " I have see you but a small time , but I put you very high . you be true , you be brave ; in time I think you will be more of a man yet . I will be proud to hear of that . if you should speed bad , if it will come to fall as we be afraid o well ! think you have the one friend . long after you be dead and I an old wife , I will be tell the bairn about David Balfour , and my tear run . I will be tell how we part , and what I say to you , and do to you . God go with you and guide you , pray your little friend : so I say I will be tell they and here be what I do . " 

 she take up my hand and kiss it . this so surprise my spirit that I cry out like one hurt . the colour come strong in her face , and she look at I and nod . 

 " o yes , Mr. David , " say she , " that be what I think of you . the head go with the lip . " 

 I could read in her face high spirit , and a chivalry like a brave child s ; not anything besides . she kiss my hand , as she have kiss Prince Charlie s , with a high passion than the common kind of clay have any sense of . nothing before have teach I how deep I be her lover , nor how far I have yet to climb to make she think of I in such a character . yet I could tell myself I have advance some way , and that her heart have beat and her blood flow at thought of I . 

 after that honour she have do I I could offer no more trivial civility . it be even hard for I to speak ; a certain lifting in her voice have knock directly at the door of my own tear . 

 " I praise God for your kindness , dear , " say I. " Farewell , my little friend ! " give she that name which she have give to herself ; with which I bow and leave she . 

 my way be down the glen of the Leith River , towards Stockbridge and Silvermills . a path lead in the foot of it , the water bicker and sing in the midst ; the sunbeam overhead strike out of the west among long shadow and   as the valley turn   make like a new scene and a new world of it at every corner . with Catriona behind and Alan before I , I be like one lift up . the place besides , and the hour , and the talking of the water , infinitely please I ; and I linger in my step and look before and behind I as I go . this be the cause , under Providence , that I spy a little in my rear a red head among some bush . 

 anger spring in my heart , and I turn straight about and walk at a stiff pace to where I come from . the path lie close by the bush where I have remark the head . the cover come to the wayside , and as I pass I be all string up to meet and to resist an onfall . no such thing befell , I go by unmeddled with ; and at that fear increase upon I . it be still day indeed , but the place exceed solitary . if my haunter have let slip that fair occasion I could but judge they aim at something more than David Balfour . the life of Alan and James weigh upon my spirit with the weight of two grow bullock . 

 Catriona be yet in the garden walk by herself . 

 " Catriona , " say I , " you see I back again . " 

 " with a changed face , " say she . 

 " I carry two man s life besides my own , " say I. " it would be a sin and shame not to walk carefully . I be doubtful whether I do right to come here . I would like it ill , if it be by that mean we be bring to harm . " 

 " I could tell you one that would be like it less , and will like little enough to hear you talk at this very same time , " she cry . " what have I do , at all event ? " 

 " o , you I you be not alone , " I reply . " but since I go off I have be dog again , and I can give you the name of he that follow I . it be Neil , son of Duncan , your man or your father s. " 

 " to be sure you be mistaken there , " she say , with a white face . " Neil be in Edinburgh on errand from my father . " 

 " it be what I fear , " say I , " the last of it . but for his be in Edinburgh I think I can show you another of that . for sure you have some signal , a signal of need , such as would bring he to your help , if he be anywhere within the reach of ear and leg ? " 

 " why , how will you know that ? " say she . 

 " by mean of a magical talisman God give to I when I be bear , and the name they call it by be common - sense , " say I. " Oblige I so far as make your signal , and I will show you the red head of Neil . " 

 no doubt but I speak bitter and sharp . my heart be bitter . I blame myself and the girl and hat both of we : she for the vile crew that she be come of , myself for my wanton folly to have stick my head in such a byke of wasp . 

 Catriona set her finger to her lip and whistle once , with an exceed clear , strong , mount note , as full as a ploughman s. a while we stand silent ; and I be about to ask she to repeat the same , when I hear the sound of some one burst through the bush below on the braeside . I point in that direction with a smile , and presently Neil leap into the garden . his eye burn , and he have a black knife   as they call it on the Highland side   naked in his hand ; but , see I beside his mistress , stand like a man strike . 

 " he have come to your call , " say I ; " judge how near he be to Edinburgh , or what be the nature of your father s errand . ask himself . if I be to lose my life , or the life of those that hang by I , through the mean of your clan , let I go where I have to go with my eye open . " 

 she address he tremulously in the Gaelic . Remembering Alan s anxious civility in that particular , I could have laugh out loud for bitterness ; here , sure , in the midst of these suspicion , be the hour she should have stick by English . 

 twice or thrice they speak together , and I could make out that Neil   for all his obsequiousness   be an angry man . 

 then she turn to I . " he swear it be not , " she say . 

 " Catriona , " say I , " do you believe the man yourself ? " 

 she make a gesture like wring the hand . 

 " how will I can know ? " she cry . 

 " but I must find some mean to know , " say I. " I can not continue to go dovere round in the black night with two man s life at my girdle ! Catriona , try to put yourself in my place , as I vow to God I try hard to put myself in your . this be no kind of talk that should ever have fall between I and you ; no kind of talk ; my heart be sick with it . see , keep he here till two of the morning , and I care not . try he with that . " 

 they speak together once more in the Gaelic . 

 " he say he have James more my father s errand , " say she . she be white than ever , and her voice falter as she say it . 

 " it be pretty plain now , " say I , " and may God forgive the wicked ! " 

 she say never anything to that , but continue gaze at I with the same white face . 

 " this be a fine business , " say I again . " be I to fall , then , and those two along with I ? " 

 " o , what be I to do ? " she cry . " could I go against my father s order , he in prison , in the danger of his life ! " 

 " but perhaps we go too fast , " say I. " this may be a lie too . he may have no right order ; all may be contrive by Simon , and your father know nothing . " 

 she burst out weeping between the pair of we ; and my heart smite I hard , for I think this girl be in a dreadful situation . 

 " here , " say I , " keep he but the one hour ; and I ll chance it , and may God bless you . " 

 she put out her hand to I , " I will he need one good word , " she sob . 

 " the full hour , then ? " say I , keep her hand in mine . " three life of it , my lass ! " 

 " the full hour ! " she say , and cry aloud on her Redeemer to forgive she . 

 I think it no fit place for I , and flee . 

 CHAPTER XI the wood by SILVERMILLS 

 I lose no time , but down through the valley and by Stockbridge and Silvermills as hard as I could stave . it be Alan s tryst to be every night between twelve and two " in a bit scrog of wood by east of Silvermills and by south the south mill - lade . " this I find easy enough , where it grow on a steep brae , with the mill - lade flow swift and deep along the foot of it ; and here I begin to walk slow and to reflect more reasonably on my employment . I see I have make but a fool s bargain with Catriona . it be not to be suppose that Neil be send alone upon his errand , but perhaps he be the only man belong to James More ; in which case I should have do all I could to hang Catriona s father , and nothing the least material to help myself . to tell the truth , I fancy neither one of these idea . suppose by hold back Neil , the girl should have help to hang her father , I think she would never forgive herself this side of time . and suppose there be other pursue I that moment , what kind of a gift be I come bring to Alan ? and how would I like that ? 

 I be up with the west end of that wood when these two consideration strike I like a cudgel . my foot stop of themselves and my heart along with they . " what wild game be this that I have be play ? " think I ; and turn instantly upon my heel to go elsewhere . 

 this bring my face to Silvermills ; the path come past the village with a crook , but all plainly visible ; and , Highland or Lowland , there be nobody stir . here be my advantage , here be just such a conjuncture as Stewart have counsel I to profit by , and I run by the side of the mill - lade , fetch about beyond the east corner of the wood , thread through the midst of it , and return to the west selvage , whence I could again command the path , and yet be myself unseen . again it be all empty , and my heart begin to rise . 

 for more than an hour I sit close in the border of the tree , and no hare or eagle could have keep a more particular watch . when that hour begin the sun be already set , but the sky still all golden and the daylight clear ; before the hour be do it have fall to be half mirk , the image and distance of thing be mingle , and observation begin to be difficult . all that time not a foot of man have come east from Silvermills , and the few that have go west be honest countryfolk and their wife upon the road to bed . if I be track by the most cunning spy in Europe , I judge it be beyond the course of nature they could have any jealousy of where I be : and go a little further home into the wood I lie down to wait for Alan . 

 the strain of my attention have be great , for I have watch not the path only , but every bush and field within my vision . that be now at an end . the moon , which be in her first quarter , glint a little in the wood ; all round there be a stillness of the country ; and as I lay there on my back , the next three or four hour , I have a fine occasion to review my conduct . 

 two thing become plain to I first : that I have no right to go that day to Dean , and   have go there   have now no right to be lie where I be . this   where Alan be to come   be just the one wood in all broad Scotland that be , by every proper feeling , close against I ; I admit that , and yet stay on , wonder at myself . I think of the measure with which I have mete to Catriona that same night ; how I have prate of the two life I carry , and have thus force she to enjeopardy her father s ; and how I be here expose they again , it seem in wantonness . a good conscience be eight part of courage . no soon have I lose conceit of my behaviour , than I seem to stand disarm amidst a throng of terror . of a sudden I sit up . how if I go now to Prestongrange , catch he   as I still easily might   before he sleep , and make a full submission ? who could blame I ? not Stewart the writer ; I have but to say that I be follow , despair of get clear , and so give in . not Catriona : here , too , I have my answer ready ; that I could not bear she should expose her father . so , in a moment , I could lay all these trouble by , which be after all and truly none of mine ; swim clear of the Appin murder ; get forth out of hand - stroke of all the Stewarts and Campbells , all the Whigs and Tories , in the land ; and live henceforth to my own mind , and be able to enjoy and to improve my fortune , and devote some hour of my youth to court Catriona , which would be surely a more suitable occupation than to hide and run and be follow like a hunted thief , and begin over again the dreadful misery of my escape with Alan . 

 at first I think no shame of this capitulation ; I be only amazed I have not think upon the thing and do it early ; and begin to inquire into the cause of the change . these I trace to my lowness of spirit , that back to my late recklessness , and that again to the common , old , public , disconsidere sin of self - indulgence . instantly the text come in my head , " how can Satan cast out Satan ? " what ?   I think   I have , by self - indulgence ; and the following of pleasant path , and the lure of a young maid , cast myself wholly out of conceit with my own character , and jeopardise the life of James and Alan ? and I be to seek the way out by the same road as I have enter in ? no ; the hurt that have be cause by self - indulgence must be cure by self - denial ; the flesh I have pamper must be crucify . I look about I for that course which I least like to follow : this be to leave the wood without wait to see Alan , and go forth again alone , in the dark and in the midst of my perplexed and dangerous fortune . 

 I have be the more careful to narrate this passage of my reflection , because I think it be of some utility , and may serve as an example to young man . but there be reason   they say   in plant kale , and even in ethic and religion , room for common sense . it be already close on Alan s hour , and the moon be down . if I leave   as I could not very decently whistle to my spy to follow I   they might miss I in the dark and tack themselves to Alan by mistake . if I stay , I could at the least of it set my friend upon his guard which might prove his mere salvation . I have adventure other people safety in a course of self - indulgence ; to have endanger they again , and now on a mere design of penance , would have be scarce rational . accordingly , I have scarce rise from my place ere I sit down again , but already in a different frame of spirit , and equally marvel at my past weakness and rejoice in my present composure . 

 presently after come a crackling in the thicket . put my mouth near down to the ground , I whistle a note or two , of Alan s air ; an answer come in the like guard tone , and soon we have knock together in the dark . 

 " be this you at last , Davie ? " he whisper . 

 " just myself , " say I. 

 " God , man , but I ve be weary to see ye ! " say he . " I ve have the long kind of a time . a day , I ve have my dwelling into the inside of a stack of hay , where I couldnae see the nebs of my ten finger ; and then two hour of it wait here for you , and you never come ! dod , and ye re none too soon the way it be , with I to sail the morn ! the morn ? what be I say ? the day , I mean . " 

 " ay , Alan , man , the day , sure enough , " say I. " it s past twelve now , surely , and ye sail the day . this ll be a long road you have before you . " 

 " we ll have a long crack of it first , " say he . 

 " well , indeed , and I have a good deal it will be tell you to hear , " say I. 

 and I tell he what behoove , make rather a jumble of it , but clear enough when do . he hear I out with very few question , laugh here and there like a man delight : and the sound of his laughing   above all there , in the dark , where neither one of we could see the other   be extraordinary friendly to my heart . 

 " ay , Davie , ye re a queer character , " say he , when I have do : " a queer bitch after a , and I have no mind of meet with the like of ye . as for your story , Prestongrange be a Whig like yoursel , so I ll say the less of he ; and , dod ! I believe he be the good friend ye have , if ye could only trust he . but Simon Fraser and James More be my ain kind of cattle , and I ll give they the name that they deserve . the muckle black deil be father to the Frasers , a body ken that ; and as for the Gregara , I never could abye the reek of they since I could stotter on two foot . I bloody the nose of one , I mind , when I be still so wambly on my leg that I cowpe upon the top of he . a proud man be my father that day , God rest he ! and I think he have the cause . I ll never can deny but what Robin be something of a piper , " he add ; " but as for James More , the deil guide he for I ! " 

 " one thing we have to consider , " say I. " be Charles Stewart right or wrong ? be it only I they re after , or the pair of we ? " 

 " and what s your ain opinion , you that s a man of so much experience ? " say he . 

 " it pass I , " say I. 

 " and I too , " say Alan . " do ye think this lass would keep her word to ye ? " he ask . 

 " I do that , " say I. 

 " well , there s nae telling , " say he . " and anyway , that s over and do : he ll be join to the rest of they lang syne . " 

 " how many would ye think there would be of they ? " I ask . 

 " that depend , " say Alan . " if it be only you , they would likely send two - three lively , brisk young birkie , and if they think that I be to appear in the employ , I daresay ten or twelve , " say he . 

 it be no use , I give a little crack of laughter . 

 " and I think your own two eye will have see I drive that number , or the double of it , near hand ! " cry he . 

 " it matter the less , " say I , " because I be well rid of they for this time . " 

 " Nae doubt that s your opinion , " say he ; " but I wouldnae be the least surprised if they be hunker this wood . ye see , David man ; they ll be Hieland folk . there ll be some fraser , I m think , and some of the Gregara ; and I would never deny but what the both of they , and the Gregara in especial , be clever experienced person . a man ken little till he s drive a spreagh of neat cattle   say   ten mile through a throng lowland country and the black soldier maybe at his tail . it s there that I learn a great part of my penetration . and ye need nae tell I : it s well than war ; which be the next good , however , though generally rather a bauchle of a business . now the Gregara have have grand practice . " 

 " no doubt that s a branch of education that be leave out with I , " say I. 

 " and I can see the mark of it upon ye constantly , " say Alan . " but that s the strange thing about you folk of the college learning : ye re ignorat , and ye cannae see t. Wae s I for my Greek and Hebrew ; but , man , I ken that I dinnae ken they there s the differ of it . now , here s you . ye lie on your wame a bittie in the bield of this wood , and ye tell I that ye ve cuist off these Frasers and Macgregors . why ? because I couldnae see they , say you . ye blockhead , that s their livelihood . " 

 " take the bad of it , " say I , " and what be we to do ? " 

 " I be think of that same , " say he . " we might twine . it wouldnae be greatly to my taste ; and forbye that , I see reason against it . first , it s now unco dark , and it s just humanly possible we might give they the clean slip . if we keep together , we make but the ae line of it ; if we gang separate , we make twae of they : the more likelihood to stave in upon some of these gentry of your . and then , second , if they keep the track of we , it may come to a fecht for it yet , Davie ; and then , I ll confess I would be blythe to have you at my oxter , and I think you would be none the bad of have I at your . so , by my way of it , we should creep out of this wood no far go than just the inside of next minute , and hold away east for Gillane , where I m to find my ship . it ll be like old day while it last , Davie ; and   come the time   we ll have to think what you should be do . I m wae to leave ye here , want I . " 

 " have with ye , then ! " say I. " do ye gang back where you be stop ? " 

 " deil a fear ! " say Alan . " they be good folk to I , but I think they would be a good deal disappoint if they see my bonny face again . for   the way time go   I be nae just what ye could call a Walcome Guest . which make I the keener for your company , Mr. David Balfour of the Shaws , and set ye up ! for , leave aside twa crack here in the wood with Charlie Stewart , I have scarce say black or white since the day we part at Corstorphine . " 

 with which he rise from his place , and we begin to move quietly eastward through the wood . 

 CHAPTER XII on the MARCH again with ALAN 

 it be likely between one and two ; the moon   as I have say   be down ; a strongish wind , carry a heavy wrack of cloud , have set in suddenly from the west ; and we begin our movement in as black a night as ever a fugitive or a murderer want . the whiteness of the path guide we into the sleep town of Broughton , thence through Picardy , and beside my old acquaintance the gibbet of the two thief . a little beyond we make a useful beacon , which be a light in an upper window of Lochend . steer by this , but a good deal at random , and with some trampling of the harvest , and stumble and fall down upon the bank , we make our way across country , and win forth at last upon the linky , boggy muirland that they call the Figgate Whins . here , under a bush of whin , we lie down the remainder of that night and slumber . 

 the day call we about five . a beautiful morning it be , the high westerly wind still blow strong , but the cloud all blow away to Europe . Alan be already sit up and smile to himself . it be my first sight of my friend since we be part , and I look upon he with enjoyment . he have still the same big great - coat on his back ; but   what be new   he have now a pair of knitted boot - hose draw above the knee . Doubtless these be intend for disguise ; but , as the day promise to be warm , he make a most unseasonable figure . 

 " well , Davie , " say he , " be this no a bonny morning ? here be a day that look the way that a day ought to . this be a great change of it from the belly of my haystack ; and while you be there sottere and sleep I have do a thing that maybe I do very seldom . " 

 " and what be that ? " say I. 

 " o , just say my prayer , " say he . 

 " and where be my gentry , as ye call they ? " I ask . 

 " Gude ken , " say he ; " and the short and the long of it be that we must take our chance of they . up with your foot - sol , Davie ! Forth , Fortune , once again of it ! and a bonny walk we be like to have . " 

 so we go east by the beach of the sea , towards where the salt - pan be smoke in by the Esk mouth . no doubt there be a by - ordinary bonny blink of morning sun on Arthur s Seat and the green Pentlands ; and the pleasantness of the day appear to set Alan among nettle . 

 " I feel like a gomeral , " say he , " to be leave Scotland on a day like this . it stick in my head ; I would maybe like it well to stay here and hing . " 

 " ay , but ye wouldnae , Alan , " say I. 

 " no , but what France be a good place too , " he explain ; " but it s some way no the same . it s brawer I believe , but it s no Scotland . I like it fine when I m there , man ; yet I kind of weary for scot divot and the Scots peat - reek . " 

 " if that s all you have to complain of , Alan , it s no such great affair , " say I. 

 " and it set I ill to be complain , whatever , " say he , " and I but new out of yon deil s haystack . " 

 " and so you be unco weary of your haystack ? " I ask . 

 " Weary s nae word for it , " say he . " I m not just precisely a man that s easily cast down ; but I do well with caller air and the lift above my head . I m like the auld Black Douglas   wasnae t ?   that likit well to hear the laverock sing than the mouse cheep . and yon place , ye see , Davie whilk be a very suitable place to hide in , as I m free to own be pit mirk from dawn to gloame . there be day   or night , for how would I tell one from other ?   that seem to I as long as a long winter . " 

 " how do you know the hour to bide your tryst ? " I ask . 

 " the goodman bring I my meat and a drop brandy , and a candle - dowp to eat it by , about eleeven , " say he . " so , when I have swallow a bit , it would he time to be get to the wood . there I lay and weary for ye sore , Davie , " say he , lay his hand on my shoulder " and guess when the two hour would be about by unless Charlie Stewart would come and tell I on his watch and then back to the doom haystack . na , it be a driech employ , and praise the Lord that I have warstle through with it ! " 

 " what do you do with yourself ? " I ask . 

 " Faith , " say he , " the good I could ! while I play at the knucklebone . I m an extraordinar good hand at the knucklebone , but it s a poor piece of business play with naebody to admire ye . and while I would make song . " 

 " what be they about ? " say I. 

 " o , about the deer and the heather , " say he , " and about the ancient old chief that be all by with it lang syne , and just about what song be about in general . and then while I would make believe I have a set of pipe and I be play . I play some grand spring , and I think I play they awful bonny ; I vow while that I could hear the squeal of they ! but the great affair be that it s do with . " 

 with that he carry I again to my adventure , which he hear all over again with more particularity , and extraordinary approval , swear at interval that I be " a queer character of a callant . " 

 " so ye be frich ene of Sim Fraser ? " he ask once . 

 " in troth be I ! " cry I. 

 " so would I have be , Davie , " say he . " and that be indeed a driedful man . but it be only proper to give the deil his due : and I can tell you he be a most respectable person on the field of war . " 

 " be he so brave ? " I ask . 

 " Brave ! " say he . " he be as brave as my steel sword . " 

 the story of my duel set he beside himself . 

 " to think of that ! " he cry . " I show ye the trick in Corrynakiegh too . and three time three time disarm ! it s a disgrace upon my character that learn ye ! here , stand up , out with your airn ; ye shall walk no step beyond this place upon the road till ye can do yoursel and I mair credit . " 

 " Alan , " say I , " this be midsummer madness . here be no time for fence lesson . " 

 " I cannae well say no to that , " he admit . " but three time , man ! and you stand there like a straw bogle and rinne to fetch your ain sword like a doggie with a pocket - napkin ! David , this man Duncansby must be something altogether by - ordinar ! he maun be extraordinar skilly . if I have the time , I would gang straight back and try a turn at he mysel . the man must be a provost . " 

 " you silly fellow , " say I , " you forget it be just I . " 

 " na , " say he , " but three time ! " 

 " when ye ken yourself that I be fair incompetent , " I cry . 

 " well , I never hear tell the equal of it , " say he . 

 " I promise you the one thing , Alan , " say I. " the next time that we forgather , I ll be well learn . you shall not continue to bear the disgrace of a friend that can not strike . " 

 " ay , the next time ! " say he . " and when will that be , I would like to ken ? " 

 " well , Alan , I have have some thought of that , too , " say I ; " and my plan be this . it s my opinion to be call an advocate . " 

 " that s but a weary trade , Davie , " say Alan , " and rather a blagyard one forby . Ye would be well in a king s coat than that . " 

 " and no doubt that would be the way to have we meet , " cry I. " but as you ll be in King Lewie s coat , and I ll be in King Geordie s , we ll have a dainty meeting of it . " 

 " there s some sense in that , " he admit . 

 " an advocate , then , it ll have to be , " I continue , " and I think it a more suitable trade for a gentleman that be three time disarm . but the beauty of the thing be this : that one of the good college for that kind of learning and the one where my kinsman , Pilrig , make his study be the college of Leyden in Holland . now , what say you , Alan ? could not a cadet of Royal Ecossais get a furlough , slip over the march , and call in upon a Leyden student ? " 

 " well , and I would think he could ! " cry he . " ye see , I stand well in with my colonel , Count Drummond - Melfort ; and , what s mair to the purpose I have a cousin of mine lieutenant - colonel in a regiment of the Scots - Dutch . naething could be mair proper than what I would get a leave to see Lieutenant - Colonel Stewart of Halkett s. and Lord Melfort , who be a very scienteefic kind of a man , and write book like Casar , would be doubtless very pleased to have the advantage of my observe . " 

 " be Lord Meloort an author , then ? " I ask , for much as Alan think of soldier , I think more of the gentry that write book . 

 " the very same , Davie , " say he . " one would think a colonel would have something well to attend to . but what can I say that make song ? " 

 " well , then , " say I , " it only remain you should give I an address to write you at in France ; and as soon as I be get to Leyden I will send you mine . " 

 " the good will be to write I in the care of my chieftain , " say he , " Charles Stewart , of Ardsheil , Esquire , at the town of Melons , in the Isle of France . it might take long , or it might take short , but it would aye get to my hand at the last of it . " 

 we have a haddock to our breakfast in Musselburgh , where it amuse I vastly to hear Alan . his great - coat and boot - hose be extremely remarkable this warm morning , and perhaps some hint of an explanation have be wise ; but Alan go into that matter like a business , or I should rather say , like a diversion . he engage the goodwife of the house with some compliment upon the rizzoring of our haddock ; and the whole of the rest of our stay hold she in talk about a cold he have take on his stomach , gravely relate all manner of symptom and suffering , and hear with a vast show of interest all the old wife remedy she could supply he with in return . 

 we leave Musselburgh before the first ninepenny coach be due from Edinburgh for   as Alan say   that be a rencounter we might very well avoid . the wind although still high , be very mild , the sun shine strong , and Alan begin to suffer in proportion . from Prestonpans he have I aside to the field of Gladsmuir , where he exert himself a great deal more than needful to describe the stage of the battle . Thence , at his old round pace , we travel to Cockenzie . though they be build herring - bus there at Mrs. Cadell s , it seem a desert - like , back - go town , about half full of ruined house ; but the ale - house be clean , and Alan , who be now in a glowing heat , must indulge himself with a bottle of ale , and carry on to the new luckie with the old story of the cold upon his stomach , only now the symptom be all different . 

 I sit listen ; and it come in my mind that I have scarce ever hear he address three serious word to any woman , but he be always drolle and fleer and make a private mock of they , and yet bring to that business a remarkable degree of energy and interest . something to this effect I remark to he , when the good - wife   as chance   be call away . 

 " what do ye want ? " say he . " a man should aye put his good foot forrit with the womankind ; he should aye give they a bit of a story to divert they , the poor lamb ! it s what ye should learn to attend to , David ; ye should get the principle , it s like a trade . now , if this have be a young lassie , or onyways bonnie , she would never have hear tell of my stomach , Davie . but aince they re too old to be seek joe , they a set up to be apotecarie . why ? what do I ken ? they ll be just the way God make they , I suppose . but I think a man would be a gomeral that didnae give his attention to the same . " 

 and here , the luckie come back , he turn from I as if with impatience to renew their former conversation . the lady have branch some while before from Alan s stomach to the case of a goodbrother of her own in Aberlady , whose last sickness and demise she be describe at extraordinary length . sometimes it be merely dull , sometimes both dull and awful , for she talk with unction . the upshot be that I fall in a deep muse , look forth of the window on the road , and scarce mark what I see . presently have any be look they might have see I to start . 

 " we pit a fomentation to his foot , " the good - wife be say , " and a het stane to his wame , and we gi he hyssop and water of pennyroyal , and fine , clean balsam of sulphur for the hoast . . . " 

 " Sir , " say I , cut very quietly in , " there s a friend of mine go by the house . " 

 " be that e en sae ? " reply Alan , as though it be a thing of small account . and then , " Ye be say , mem ? " say he ; and the wearyful wife go on . 

 presently , however , he pay she with a half - crown piece , and she must go forth after the change . 

 " be it he with the red head ? " ask Alan . 

 " Ye have it , " say I. 

 " what do I tell you in the wood ? " he cry . " and yet it s strange he should be here too ! be he his lane ? " 

 " his lee - lane for what I could see , " say I. 

 " do he gang by ? " he ask . 

 " straight by , " say I , " and look neither to the right nor left . " 

 " and that s queerer yet , " say Alan . " it stick in my mind , Davie , that we should be stir . but where to ? deil hae t ! this be like old day fairly , " cry he . 

 " there be one big differ , though , " say I , " that now we have money in our pocket . " 

 " and another big differ , Mr. Balfour , " say he , " that now we have dog at our tail . they re on the scent ; they re in full cry , David . it s a bad business and be damn to it . " and he sit think hard with a look of his that I know well . 

 " I m say , Luckie , " say he , when the goodwife return , " have ye a back road out of this change house ? " 

 she tell he there be and where it lead to . 

 " then , sir , " say he to I , " I think that will be the short road for we . and here s good - bye to ye , my braw woman ; and I ll no forget thon of the cinnamon water . " 

 we go out by way of the woman s kale yard , and up a lane among field . Alan look sharply to all side , and see we be in a little hollow place of the country , out of view of man , sit down . 

 " now for a council of war , Davie , " say he . " but first of all , a bit lesson to ye . suppose that I have be like you , what would yon old wife have mind of the pair of we ! just that we have go out by the back gate . and what do she mind now ? a fine , canty , friendly , cracky man , that suffer with the stomach , poor body ! and be real ta en up about the goodbrother . o man , David , try and learn to have some kind of intelligence ! " 

 " I ll try , Alan , " say I. 

 " and now for he of the red head , " say he ; " be he gaun fast or slow ? " 

 " Betwixt and between , " say I. 

 " no kind of a hurry about the man ? " he ask . 

 " never a sign of it , " say I. 

 " Nhm ! " say Alan , " it look queer . we see nothing of they this morning on the Whins ; he s pass we by , he doesnae seem to be look , and yet here he be on our road ! Dod , Davie , I begin to take a notion . I think it s no you they re seek , I think it s I ; and I think they ken fine where they re gaun . " 

 " they ken ? " I ask . 

 " I think Andie Scougal s sell I he or his mate wha ken some part of the affair or else Charlie s clerk callant , which would be a pity too , " say Alan ; " and if you askit I for just my inward private conviction , I think there ll be head crack on Gillane sand . " 

 " Alan , " I cry , " if you re at all right there ll be folk there and to spare . it ll be small service to crack head . " 

 " it would aye be a satisfaction though , " say Alan . " but bide a bit ; bide a bit ; I m think and thank to this bonny westland wind , I believe I ve still a chance of it . it s this way , Davie . I m no trysted with this man Scougal till the gloaming come . but , " say he , " if I can get a bit of a wind out of the west I ll be there long or that , " he say , " and lie - to for ye behind the Isle of Fidra . now if your gentry ken the place , they ken the time forbye . do ye see I come , Davie ? thank to Johnnie Cope and other red - coat gomeral , I should ken this country like the back of my hand ; and if ye re ready for another bit run with Alan Breck , we ll can cast back inshore , and come to the seaside again by Dirleton . if the ship s there , we ll try and get on board of she . if she s no there , I ll just have to get back to my weary haystack . but either way of it , I think we will leave your gentry whistle on their thumb . " 

 " I believe there s some chance in it , " say I. " have on with ye , Alan ! " 

 CHAPTER XIII GILLANE sand 

 I do not profit by Alan s pilotage as he have do by his marching under General Cope ; for I can scarce tell what way we go . it be my excuse that we travel exceed fast . some part we run , some trot , and the rest walk at a vengeance of a pace . twice , while we be at top speed , we run against country - folk ; but though we plump into the first from round a corner , Alan be as ready as a loaded musket . 

 " have ye see my horse ? " he gasp . 

 " Na , man , I haenae see nae horse the day , " reply the countryman . 

 and Alan spar the time to explain to he that we be travel " ride and tie " ; that our charger have escape , and it be fear he have go home to Linton . not only that , but he expend some breath   of which he have not very much leave   to curse his own misfortune and my stupidity which be say to be its cause . 

 " they that cannae tell the truth , " he observe to myself as we go on again , " should be aye mindful to leave an honest , handy lee behind they . if folk dinnae ken what ye re do , Davie , they re terrible take up with it ; but if they think they ken , they care nae mair for it than what I do for pease porridge . " 

 as we have first make inland , so our road come in the end to lie very near due north ; the old Kirk of Aberlady for a landmark on the left ; on the right , the top of the Berwick Law ; and it be thus we strike the shore again , not far from Dirleton . from north Berwick west to Gillane Ness there run a string of four small islet , Craiglieth , the Lamb , Fidra , and Eyebrough , notable by their diversity of size and shape . Fidra be the most particular , be a strange grey islet of two hump , make the more conspicuous by a piece of ruin ; and I mind that   as we draw close to it   by some door or window of these ruin the sea peep through like a man s eye . under the lee of Fidra there be a good anchorage in westerly wind , and there , from a far way off , we could see the thistle riding . 

 the shore in face of these islet be altogether waste . here be no dwelling of man , and scarce any passage , or at most of vagabond child run at their play . gillane be a small place on the far side of the Ness , the folk of Dirleton go to their business in the inland field , and those of North Berwick straight to the sea - fishing from their haven ; so that few part of the coast be lonely . but I mind , as we crawl upon our belly into that multiplicity of height and hollow , keep a bright eye upon all side , and our heart hammer at our rib , there be such a shining of the sun and the sea , such a stir of the wind in the bent grass , and such a bustle of down - pop rabbit and up - fly gull , that the desert seem to I , like a place alive . no doubt it be in all way well choose for a secret embarcation , if the secret have be keep ; and even now that it be out , and the place watch , we be able to creep unperceive to the front of the sandhill , where they look down immediately on the beach and sea . 

 but here Alan come to a full stop . 

 " Davie , " say he , " this be a kittle passage ! as long as we lie here we re safe ; but I m nane sae muckle nearer to my ship or the coast of France . and as soon as we stand up and signal the brig , it s another matter . for where will your gentry be , think ye ? " 

 " maybe they re no come yet , " say I. " and even if they be , there s one clear matter in our favour . they ll be all arrange to take we , that s true . but they ll have arrange for our come from the east and here we be upon their west . " 

 " ay , " say Alan , " I wish we be in some force , and this be a battle , we would have bonnily out - manouvre they ! but it isnae , Davit ; and the way it be , be a wee thing less inspiring to Alan Breck . I swither , Davie . " 

 " time fly , Alan , " say I. 

 " I ken that , " say Alan . " I ken naethe else , as the french folk say . but this be a dreidful case of heid or tail . o ! if I could but ken where your gentry be ! " 

 " Alan , " say I , " this be no like you . it s get to be now or never . " 

 " this be no I , quo he , " 

 sing Alan , with a queer face betwixt shame and drollery . 

 " neither you nor I , quo he , neither you nor I . 
 wow , na , Johnnie man ! neither you nor I . " 

 and then of a sudden he stand straight up where he be , and with a handkerchief fly in his right hand , march down upon the beach . I stand up myself , but linger behind he , scan the sand - hill to the east . his appearance be at first unremarked : Scougal not expect he so early , and my gentry watch on the other side . then they awake on board the Thistle , and it seem they have all in readiness , for there be scarce a second s bustle on the deck before we see a skiff put round her stern and begin to pull lively for the coast . almost at the same moment of time , and perhaps half a mile away towards Gillane Ness , the figure of a man appear for a blink upon a sandhill , wave with his arm ; and though he be go again in the same flash , the gull in that part continue a little long to fly wild . 

 Alan have not see this , look straight to seaward at the ship and skiff . 

 " it maun be as it will ! " say he , when I have tell he , " Weel may yon boatie row , or my craig ll have to thole a raxing . " 

 that part of the beach be long and flat , and excellent walking when the tide be down ; a little cressy burn flow over it in one place to the sea ; and the sandhill run along the head of it like the rampart of a town . no eye of ours could spy what be pass behind there in the bent , no hurry of ours could mend the speed of the boat s come : time stand still with we through that uncanny period of wait . 

 " there be one thing I would like to ken , " say Alan . " I would like to ken these gentry s order . we re worth four hunner pound the pair of we : how if they take the gun to we , Davie ! they would get a bonny shot from the top of that lang sandy bank . " 

 " morally impossible , " say I. " the point be that they can have no gun . this thing have be go about too secret ; pistol they may have , but never gun . " 

 " I believe ye ll be in the right , " say Alan . " for all which I be wear a good deal for yon boat . " 

 and he snap his finger and whistle to it like a dog . 

 it be now perhaps a third of the way in , and we ourselves already hard on the margin of the sea , so that the soft sand rise over my shoe . there be no more to do whatever but to wait , to look as much as we be able at the creep nearer of the boat , and as little as we could manage at the long impenetrable front of the sandhill , over which the gull twinkle and behind which our enemy be doubtless marshalling . 

 " this be a fine , bright , caller place to get shoot in , " say Alan suddenly ; " and , man , I wish that I have your courage ! " 

 " Alan ! " I cry , " what kind of talk be this of it ! you re just make of courage ; it s the character of the man , as I could prove myself if there be nobody else . " 

 " and you would be the more mistaken , " say he . " what make the differ with I be just my great penetration and knowledge of affair . but for auld , cauld , dour , deadly courage , I be not fit to hold a candle to yourself . look at we two here upon the sand . here be I , fair hotching to be off ; here s you   for all that I ken   in two mind of it whether you ll no stop . do you think that I could do that , or would ? no I ! firstly , because I havenae get the courage and wouldnae daur ; and secondly , because I be a man of so much penetration and would see ye damn first . " 

 " it s there ye re come , be it ? " I cry . " ah , man Alan , you can wile your old wife , but you never can wile I . " 

 remembrance of my temptation in the wood make I strong as iron . 

 " I have a tryst to keep , " I continue . " I be tryste with your cousin Charlie ; I have pass my word . " 

 " braw tryst that you ll can keep , " say Alan . " Ye ll just mistryst aince and for a with the gentry in the bent . and what for ? " he go on with an extreme threaten gravity . " just tell I that , my mannie ! be ye to be speerite away like Lady Grange ? be they to drive a dirk in your inside and bury ye in the bent ? or be it to be the other way , and be they to bring ye in with James ? be they folk to be trustit ? would ye stick your head in the mouth of Sim Fraser and the ither whig ? " he add with extraordinary bitterness . 

 " Alan , " cry I , " they re all rogue and liar , and I m with ye there . the more reason there should be one decent man in such a land of thief ! my word be pass , and I ll stick to it . I say long syne to your kinswoman that I would stumble at no risk . do ye mind of that ? the night Red Colin fall , it be . no more I will , then . here I stop . Prestongrange promise I my life : if he s to be mansworn , here I ll have to die . " 

 " Aweel aweel , " say Alan . 

 all this time we have see or hear no more of our pursuer . in truth we have catch they unawares ; their whole party   as I be to learn afterwards   have not yet reach the scene ; what there be of they be spread among the bent towards Gillane . it be quite an affair to call they in and bring they over , and the boat be make speed . they be besides but cowardly fellow : a mere leash of Highland cattle - thief , of several clan , no gentleman there to be the captain and the more they look at Alan and I upon the beach , the less   I must suppose   they like the look of we . 

 whoever have betray Alan it be not the captain : he be in the skiff himself , steer and stir up his oarsman , like a man with his heart in his employ . already he be near in , and the boat secure already Alan s face have flame crimson with the excitement of his deliverance , when our friend in the bent , either in their despair to see their prey escape they or with some hope of scar Andie , raise suddenly a shrill cry of several voice . 

 this sound , arise from what appear to be a quite deserted coast , be really very daunting , and the man in the boat hold water instantly . 

 " what s this of it ? " sing out the captain , for he be come within an easy hail . 

 " freen o mine , " say Alan , and begin immediately to wade forth in the shallow water towards the boat . " Davie , " he say , pausing , " Davie , be ye no coming ? I be swi to leave ye . " 

 " not a hair of I , " say I. 

 " he stand part of a second where he be to his knee in the salt water , hesitate . 

 " he that will to Cupar , maun to Cupar , " say he , and swash in deep than his waist , be haul into the skiff , which be immediately direct for the ship . 

 I stand where he have leave I , with my hand behind my back ; Alan sit with his head turn watch I ; and the boat draw smoothly away . of a sudden I come the near hand to shed tear , and seem to myself the most deserted solitary lad in Scotland . with that I turn my back upon the sea and face the sandhill . there be no sight or sound of man ; the sun shine on the wet sand and the dry , the wind blow in the bent , the gull make a dreary piping . as I pass higher up the beach , the sand - lice be hop nimbly about the strand tangle . the devil any other sight or sound in that unchancy place . and yet I know there be folk there , observe I , upon some secret purpose . they be no soldier , or they would have fall on and take we ere now ; doubtless they be some common rogue hire for my undoing , perhaps to kidnap , perhaps to murder I outright . from the position of those engage , the first be the more likely ; from what I know of their character and ardency in this business , I think the second very possible ; and the blood run cold about my heart . 

 I have a mad idea to loosen my sword in the scabbard ; for though I be very unfit to stand up like a gentleman blade to blade , I think I could do some scathe in a random combat . but I perceive in time the folly of resistance . this be no doubt the joint " expedient " on which Prestongrange and Fraser be agree . the first , I be very sure , have do something to secure my life ; the second be pretty likely to have slip in some contrary hint into the ear of Neil and his companion ; and if I be to show bare steel I might play straight into the hand of my bad enemy and seal my own doom . 

 these thought bring I to the head of the beach . I cast a look behind , the boat be near the brig , and Alan fly his handkerchief for a farewell , which I reply to with the waving of my hand . but Alan himself be shrink to a small thing in my view , alongside of this pass that lie in front of I . I set my hat hard on my head , clench my tooth , and go right before I up the face of the sand - wreath . it make a hard climb , be steep , and the sand like water underfoot . but I catch hold at last by the long bent - grass on the brae - top , and pull myself to a good footing . the same moment man stir and stand up here and there , six or seven of they , ragged - like knave , each with a dagger in his hand . the fair truth be , I shut my eye and pray . when I open they again , the rogue be creep the least thing near without speech or hurry . every eye be upon mine , which strike I with a strange sensation of their brightness , and of the fear with which they continue to approach I . I hold out my hand empty ; whereupon one ask , with a strong Highland brogue , if I surrender . 

 " under protest , " say I , " if ye ken what that mean , which I misdoubt . " 

 at that word , they come all in upon I like a flight of bird upon a carrion , seize I , take my sword , and all the money from my pocket , bind I hand and foot with some strong line , and cast I on a tussock of bent . there they sit about their captive in a part of a circle and gaze upon he silently like something dangerous , perhaps a lion or a tiger on the spring . presently this attention be relax . they draw near together , fall to speech in the Gaelic , and very cynically divide my property before my eye . it be my diversion in this time that I could watch from my place the progress of my friend s escape . I see the boat come to the brig and be hoist in , the sail fill , and the ship pass out seaward behind the isle and by North Berwick . 

 in the course of two hour or so , more and more ragged Highlandmen keep collect . Neil among the first , until the party must have number near a score . with each new arrival there be a fresh bout of talk , that sound like complaint and explanation ; but I observe one thing , none of those who come late have any share in the division of my spoil . the last discussion be very violent and eager , so that once I think they would have quarrel ; on the heel of which their company part , the bulk of they return westward in a troop , and only three , Neil and two other , remain sentry on the prisoner . 

 " I could name one who would be very ill pleased with your day s work , Neil Duncanson , " say I , when the rest have move away . 

 he assure I in answer I should be tenderly use , for he know he be " acquent wi the leddy . " 

 this be all our talk , nor do any other son of man appear upon that portion of the coast until the sun have go down among the Highland mountain , and the gloaming be begin to grow dark . at which hour I be aware of a long , lean , bony - like lothian man of a very swarthy countenance , that come towards we among the bent on a farm horse . 

 " lad , " cry he , " have ye a paper like this ? " and hold up one in his hand . Neil produce a second , which the newcomer study through a pair of horn spectacle , and say all be right and we be the folk he be seek , immediately dismount . I be then set in his place , my foot tie under the horse s belly , and we set forth under the guidance of the Lowlander . his path must have be very well choose , for we meet but one pair a pair of lover the whole way , and these , perhaps take we to be free - trader , flee on our approach . we be at one time close at the foot of Berwick Law on the south side ; at another , as we pass over some open hill , I spy the light of a clachan and the old tower of a church among some tree not far off , but too far to cry for help , if I have dream of it . at last we come again within sound of the sea . there be moonlight , though not much ; and by this I could see the three huge tower and broken battlement of Tantallon , that old chief place of the Red Douglases . the horse be picket in the bottom of the ditch to graze , and I be lead within , and forth into the court , and thence into the tumble - down stone hall . here my conductor build a brisk fire in the midst of the pavement , for there be a chill in the night . my hand be loose , I be set by the wall in the inner end , and   the Lowlander have produce provision   I be give oatmeal bread and a pitcher of french brandy . this do , I be leave once more alone with my three highlandman . they sit close by the fire drinking and talk ; the wind blow in by the breach , cast about the smoke and flame , and sing in the top of the tower ; I could hear the sea under the cliff , and , my mind be reassure as to my life , and my body and spirit weary with the day s employment , I turn upon one side and slumber . 

 I have no mean of guess at what hour I be waken , only the moon be down and the fire be low . my foot be now loose , and I be carry through the ruin and down the cliff - side by a precipitous path to where I find a fisher s boat in a haven of the rock . this I be have on board of , and we begin to put forth from the shore in a fine starlight . 

 CHAPTER XIV the BASS 

 I have no thought where they be take I ; only look here and there for the appearance of a ship ; and there run the while in my head a word of Ransome s the twenty - pounder . if I be to be expose a second time to that same former danger of the plantation , I judge it must turn ill with I ; there be no second Alan ; and no second shipwreck and spare yard to be expect now ; and I see myself hoe tobacco under the whip s lash . the thought chill I ; the air be sharp upon the water , the stretcher of the boat drench with a cold dew : and I shiver in my place beside the steersman . this be the dark man whom I have call hitherto the Lowlander ; his name be Dale , ordinarily call Black Andie . feel the thrill of my shiver , he very kindly hand I a rough jacket full of fish - scale , with which I be glad to cover myself . 

 " I thank you for this kindness , " say I , " and will make so free as to repay it with a warning . you take a high responsibility in this affair . you be not like these ignorant , barbarous highlander , but know what the law be and the risk of those that break it . " 

 " I be no just exactly what ye would can an extremist for the law , " say he , " at the good of time ; but in this business I act with a good warranty . " 

 " what be you go to do with I ? " I ask . 

 " Nae harm , " say he , " nae harm ava . Ye ll have strong freen , I m think . Ye ll be richt eneuch yet . " 

 there begin to fall a greyness on the face of the sea ; little dab of pink and red , like coal of slow fire , come in the east ; and at the same time the geese awaken , and begin cry about the top of the Bass . it be just the one crag of rock , as everybody know , but great enough to carve a city from . the sea be extremely little , but there go a hollow plowter round the base of it . with the growing of the dawn I could see it clear and clear ; the straight crag paint with sea - bird dropping like a morning frost , the slop top of it green with grass , the clan of white geese that cry about the side , and the black , broken building of the prison sit close on the sea s edge . 

 at the sight the truth come in upon I in a clap . 

 " it s there you re take I ! " I cry . 

 " just to the Bass , mannie , " say he : " Whaur the auld saint be afore ye , and I misdoubt if ye have come so fairly by your preeson . " 

 " but none dwell there now , " I cry ; " the place be long a ruin . " 

 " it ll be the mair pleisand a change for the solan geese , then , " quoth Andie dryly . 

 the day come slowly brighter I observe on the bilge , among the big stone with which fisherfolk ballast their boat , several keg and basket , and a provision of fuel . all these be discharge upon the crag . Andie , myself , and my three Highlanders   I call they mine , although it be the other way about , land along with they . the sun be not yet up when the boat move away again , the noise of the oar on the thole - pin echo from the cliff , and leave we in our singular reclusion : 

 Andie Dale be the Prefect   as I would jocularly call he   of the Bass , be at once the shepherd and the gamekeeper of that small and rich estate . he have to mind the dozen or so of sheep that feed and fatten on the grass of the sloping part of it , like beast graze the roof of a cathedral . he have charge besides of the solan geese that roost in the crag ; and from these an extraordinary income be derive . the young be dainty eating , as much as two shilling a - piece be a common price , and pay willingly by epicure ; even the grown bird be valuable for their oil and feather ; and a part of the minister s stipend of North Berwick be pay to this day in solan geese , which make it   in some folk eye   a parish to be covet . to perform these several business , as well as to protect the geese from poacher , Andie have frequent occasion to sleep and pass day together on the crag ; and we find the man at home there like a farmer in his steading . bid we all shoulder some of the package , a matter in which I make haste to bear a hand , he lead we in by a locked gate , which be the only admission to the island , and through the ruin of the fortress , to the governor s house . there we see by the ash in the chimney and a stand bed - place in one corner , that he make his usual occupation . 

 this bed he now offer I to use , say he suppose I would set up to be gentry . 

 " my gentrice have nothing to do with where I lie , " say I. " I bless God I have lie hard ere now , and can do the same again with thankfulness . while I be here , Mr. Andie , if that be your name , I will do my part and take my place beside the rest of you ; and I ask you on the other hand to spare I your mockery , which I own I like ill . " 

 he grumble a little at this speech , but seem upon reflection to approve it . indeed , he be a long - headed , sensible man , and a good Whig and Presbyterian ; read daily in a pocket Bible , and be both able and eager to converse seriously on religion , lean more than a little towards the cameronian extreme . his moral be of a more doubtful colour . I find he be deep in the free trade , and use the ruin of Tantallon for a magazine of smuggle merchandise . as for a gauger , I do not believe he value the life of one at half - a - farthing . but that part of the coast of Lothian be to this day as wild a place , and the common there as rough a crew , as any in Scotland . 

 one incident of my imprisonment be make memorable by a consequence it have long after . there be a warship at this time station in the Firth , the Seahorse , Captain Palliser . it chance she be cruise in the month of September , ply between Fife and Lothian , and sound for sunk danger . early one fine morning she be see about two mile to east of we , where she lower a boat , and seem to examine the Wildfire Rocks and Satan s Bush , famous danger of that coast . and presently after have get her boat again , she come before the wind and be head directly for the Bass . this be very troublesome to Andie and the Highlanders ; the whole business of my sequestration be design for privacy , and here , with a navy captain perhaps blunder ashore , it look to become public enough , if it be nothing bad . I be in a minority of one , I be no Alan to fall upon so many , and I be far from sure that a warship be the least likely to improve my condition . all which consider , I give Andie my parole of good behaviour and obedience , and be have briskly to the summit of the rock , where we all lay down , at the cliff s edge , in different place of observation and concealment . the Seahorse come straight on till I think she would have strike , and we   look giddily down   could see the ship s company at their quarter and hear the leadsman sing at the lead . then she suddenly wear and let fly a volley of I know not how many great gun . the rock be shake with the thunder of the sound , the smoke flow over our head , and the geese rise in number beyond computation or belief . to hear their screaming and to see the twinkling of their wing , make a most inimitable curiosity ; and I suppose it be after this somewhat childish pleasure that Captain Palliser have come so near the Bass . he be to pay dear for it in time . during his approach I have the opportunity to make a remark upon the rigging of that ship by which I ever after know it mile away ; and this be a means   under Providence   of my averting from a friend a great calamity , and inflict on Captain Palliser himself a sensible disappointment . 

 all the time of my stay on the rock we live well . we have small ale and brandy , and oatmeal , of which we make our porridge night and morning . at time a boat come from the Castleton and bring we a quarter of mutton , for the sheep upon the rock we must not touch , these be specially feed to market . the goose be unfortunately out of season , and we let they be . we fish ourselves , and yet more often make the goose to fish for we : observe one when he have make a capture and scar he from his prey ere he have swallow it . 

 the strange nature of this place , and the curiosity with which it abound , hold I busy and amuse . Escape be impossible , I be allow my entire liberty , and continually explore the surface of the isle wherever it might support the foot of man . the old garden of the prison be still to be observe , with flower and pot - herb run wild , and some ripe cherry on a bush . a little low stand a chapel or a hermit s cell ; who build or dwelt in it , none may know , and the thought of its age make a ground of many meditation . the prison , too , where I now bivouac with Highland cattle - thief , be a place full of history , both human and divine . I think it strange so many saint and martyr should have go by there so recently , and leave not so much as a leaf out of their bible , or a name carve upon the wall , while the rough soldier lad that mount guard upon the battlement have fill the neighbourhood with their memento break tobacco - pipe for the most part , and that in a surprising plenty , but also metal button from their coat . there be time when I think I could have hear the pious sound of psalm out of the martyr s dungeon , and see the soldier tramp the rampart with their glinting pipe , and the dawn rise behind they out of the North Sea . 

 no doubt it be a good deal Andie and his tale that put these fancy in my head . he be extraordinarily well acquainted with the story of the rock in all particular , down to the name of private soldier , his father have serve there in that same capacity . he be gift besides with a natural genius for narration , so that the people seem to speak and the thing to be do before your face . this gift of his and my assiduity to listen bring we the more close together . I could not honestly deny but what I like he ; I soon see that he like I ; and indeed , from the first I have set myself out to capture his good - will . an odd circumstance   to be tell presently   effect this beyond my expectation ; but even in early day we make a friendly pair to be a prisoner and his gaoler .
