 I should trifle with my conscience if I pretend my stay upon the Bass be wholly disagreeable . it seem to I a safe place , as though I be escape there out of my trouble . no harm be to be offer I ; a material impossibility , rock and the deep sea , prevent I from fresh attempt ; I feel I have my life safe and my honour safe , and there be time when I allow myself to gloat on they like steal water . at other time my thought be very different , I recall how strong I have express myself both to Rankeillor and to Stewart ; I reflect that my captivity upon the Bass , in view of a great part of the coast of Fife and Lothian , be a thing I should be think more likely to have invent than endure ; and in the eye of these two gentleman , at least , I must pass for a boaster and a coward . now I would take this lightly enough ; tell myself that so long as I stand well with Catriona Drummond , the opinion of the rest of man be but moonshine and spill water ; and thence pass off into those meditation of a lover which be so delightful to himself and must always appear so surprisingly idle to a reader . but anon the fear would take I otherwise ; I would be shake with a perfect panic of self - esteem , and these suppose hard judgment appear an injustice impossible to be support . with that another train of thought would he present , and I have scarce begin to be concern about man s judgment of myself , than I be haunt with the remembrance of James Stewart in his dungeon and the lamentation of his wife . then , indeed , passion begin to work in I ; I could not forgive myself to sit there idle : it seem   if I be a man at all   that I could fly or swim out of my place of safety ; and it be in such humour and to amuse my self - reproach that I would set the more particularly to win the good side of Andie Dale . 

 at last , when we two be alone on the summit of the rock on a bright morning , I put in some hint about a bribe . he look at I , cast back his head , and laugh out loud . 

 " ay , you re funny , Mr. Dale , " say I , " but perhaps if you ll glance an eye upon that paper you may change your note . " 

 the stupid highlander have take from I at the time of my seizure nothing but hard money , and the paper I now show Andie be an acknowledgment from the British Linen Company for a considerable sum . 

 he read it . " Troth , and ye re nane sae ill aff , " say he . 

 " I think that would maybe vary your opinion , " say I. 

 " Hout ! " say he . " it show I ye can bribe ; but I m no to be bribit . " 

 " we ll see about that yet a while , " say I. " and first , I ll show you that I know what I be talk . you have order to detain I here till after Thursday , 21st September . " 

 " ye re no a thegether wrong either , " say Andie . " I m to let you gang , bar order contrair , on Saturday , the 23rd . " 

 I could not but feel there be something extremely insidious in this arrangement . that I be to re - appear precisely in time to be too late would cast the more discredit on my tale , if I be minded to tell one ; and this screw I to fighting point . 

 " now then , Andie , you that ken the world , listen to I , and think while ye listen , " say I. " I know there be great folk in the business , and I make no doubt you have their name to go upon . I have see some of they myself since this affair begin , and say my say into their face too . but what kind of a crime would this be that I have commit ? or what kind of a process be this that I be fall under ? to be apprehend by some rag John - Hielandman on August 30th , carry to a rickle of old stone that be now neither fort nor gaol   whatever it once be   but just the gamekeeper s lodge of the Bass Rock , and set free again , September 23rd , as secretly as I be first arrest do that sound like law to you ? or do it sound like justice ? or do it not sound honestly like a piece of some low dirty intrigue , of which the very folk that meddle with it be ashamed ? " 

 " I canna gainsay ye , Shaws . it look unco underhand , " say Andie . " and werenae the folk guid sound whig and true - blue Presbyterians I would have see they ayont Jordan and Jeroozlem or I would have set hand to it . " 

 " the Master of Lovat ll be a braw Whig , " say I , " and a grand Presbyterian . " 

 " I ken naethe by he , " say he . " I hae nae troking wi Lovats . " 

 " no , it ll be Prestongrange that you ll be deal with , " say I. 

 " ah , but I ll no tell ye that , " say Andie . 

 " little need when I ken , " be my retort . 

 " there s just the ae thing ye can be fairly sure of , Shaws , " say Andie . " and that be that   try as ye please   I m no deal wi yoursel ; nor yet I amnae goin to , " he add . 

 " well , Andie , I see I ll have to be speak out plain with you , " I reply . and tell he so much as I think needful of the fact . 

 he hear I out with some serious interest , and when I have do , seem to consider a little with himself . 

 " shaw , " say he at last , " I ll deal with the naked hand . it s a queer tale , and no very creditable , the way you tell it ; and I m far frae mint that be other than the way that ye believe it . as for yoursel , ye seem to I rather a dacent - like young man . but I , that s aulder and mair judeecious , see perhaps a wee bit further forrit in the job than what ye can dae . and here the maitter clear and plain to ye . there ll be nae skaith to yoursel if I keep ye here ; far free that , I think ye ll be a hantle well by it . there ll be nae skaith to the kintry just ae mair Hielantman hangit Gude ken , a guid riddance ! on the ither hand , it would be considerable skaith to I if I would let you free . Sae , speakin as a guid Whig , an honest freen to you , and an anxious freen to my ainsel , the plain fact be that I think ye ll just have to bide here wi Andie an the solan . " 

 " Andie , " say I , lay my hand upon his knee , " this Hielantman s innocent . " 

 " ay , it s a peety about that , " say he . " but ye see , in this warld , the way God make it , we cannae just get a thing that we want . " 

 CHAPTER XV BLACK ANDIE S TALE of TOD LAPRAIK 

 I have yet say little of the Highlanders . they be all three of the follower of James More , which bind the accusation very tight about their master s neck . all understand a word or two of English , but Neil be the only one who judge he have enough of it for general converse , in which   when once he get embark   his company be often tempt to the contrary opinion . they be tractable , simple creature ; show much more courtesy than might have be expect from their raggedness and their uncouth appearance , and fall spontaneously to be like three servant for Andie and myself . 

 dwell in that isolate place , in the old fall ruin of a prison , and among endless strange sound of the sea and the sea - bird , I think I perceive in they early the effect of superstitious fear . when there be nothing do they would either lie and sleep , for which their appetite appear insatiable , or Neil would entertain the other with story which seem always of a terrifying strain . if neither of these delight be within reach if perhaps two be sleep and the third could find no mean to follow their example I would see he sit and listen and look about he in a progression of uneasiness , start , his face blench , his hand clutch , a man string like a bow . the nature of these fear I have never an occasion to find out , but the sight of they be catch , and the nature of the place that we be in favourable to alarm . I can find no word for it in the English , but Andie have an expression for it in the scot from which he never vary . 

 " ay , " he would say , " it s an unco place , the Bass . " 

 it be so I always think of it . it be an unco place by night , unco by day ; and these be unco sound , of the calling of the solan , and the plash of the sea and the rock echo , that hang continually in our ear . it be chiefly so in moderate weather . when the wave be anyway great they roar about the rock like thunder and the drum of army , dreadful but merry to hear ; and it be in the calm day that a man could daunt himself with listen not a Highlandman only , as I several time experiment on myself , so many still , hollow noise haunt and reverberate in the porch of the rock . 

 this bring I to a story I hear , and a scene I take part in , which quite change our term of living , and have a great effect on my departure . it chance one night I fall in a muse beside the fire and   that little air of Alan s come back to my memory   begin to whistle . a hand be lay upon my arm , and the voice of Neil bid I to stop , for it be not " canny music . " 

 " not canny ? " I ask . " how can that be ? " 

 " na , " say he ; " it will be make by a bogle and her want ta heid upon his body . "   13 

 " well , " say I , " there can be no bogle here , Neil ; for it s not likely they would fash themselves to frighten geese . " 

 " ay ? " say Andie , " be that what ye think of it ! but I ll can tell ye there s be waur nor bogle here . " 

 " what s waur than bogle , Andie ? " say I. 

 " Warlocks , " say he . " or a warlock at the least of it . and that s a queer tale , too , " he add . " and if ye would like , I ll tell it ye . " 

 to be sure we be all of the one mind , and even the Highlander that have the least English of the three set himself to listen with all his might . 

 the Tale of Tod Lapraik 

 my faither , Tam Dale , peace to his bane , be a wild , splore lad in his young day , wi little wisdom and little grace . he be fond of a lass and fond of a glass , and fond of a ran - dan ; but I could never hear tell that he be muckle use for honest employment . Frae ae thing to anither , he list at last for a sodger and be in the garrison of this fort , which be the first way that ony of the Dales cam to set foot upon the Bass . sorrow upon that service ! the governor brew his ain ale ; it seem it be the warst conceivable . the rock be proveesione free the shore with viver , the thing be ill - guide , and there be while when they but to fish and shoot solan for their diet . to crown a , thir be the day of the Persecution . the perishin cauld chalmer be all occupeed wi sant and martyr , the saut of the yearth , of which it wasnae worthy . and though Tam Dale carry a firelock there , a single sodger , and like a lass and a glass , as I be sayin , the mind of the man be mair just than set with his position . he have glint of the glory of the kirk ; there be while when his dander rase to see the Lord s sant misguide , and shame cover he that he should be haulde a can le   or carry a firelock   in so black a business . there be night of it when he be here on sentry , the place a wheesht , the frost o winter maybe rive in the wa s , and he would hear ane o the prisoner strike up a psalm , and the rest join in , and the bless sound rise from the different chalmer or dungeon , I would raither say so that this auld craig in the sea be like a pairt of Heev n. Black shame be on his saul ; his sin hove up before he muckle as the Bass , and above a , that chief sin , that he should have a hand in hagge and hash at Christ s Kirk . but the truth be that he resist the spirit . day cam , there be the rouse compainion , and his guid resolve depairtit . 

 in thir day , dwalle upon the Bass a man of God , Peden the Prophet be his name . Ye ll have hear tell of Prophet Peden . there be never the wale of he sinsyne , and it s a question wi mony if there ever be his like afore . he be wild s a peat - hag , fearsome to look at , fearsome to hear , his face like the day of judgment . the voice of he be like a solan s and dinnle d in folk lug , and the word of he like coal of fire . 

 now there be a lass on the rock , and I think she have little to do , for it be nae place far decent weeman ; but it seem she be bonny , and she and Tam Dale be very well agree . it befell that Peden be in the gairden his lane at the praying when Tam and the lass cam by ; and what should the lassie do but mock with laughter at the sant s devotion ? he rise and lookit at the twa o they , and Tam s knee knoitere thegether at the look of he . but whan he spak , it be mair in sorrow than in anger . " poor thing , poor thing ! " say he , and it be the lass he lookit at , " I hear you skirl and laugh , " he say , " but the Lord have a deid shot prepare for you , and at that surprising judgment ye shall skirl but the ae time ! " shortly thereafter she be daundere on the craig wi twa - three sodger , and it be a blawy day . there cam a gowst of wind , claught she by the coat , and awa wi her bag and baggage . and it be remark by the sodger that she gi but the ae skirl . 

 Nae doubt this judgment have some weicht upon Tam Dale ; but it pass again and he none the well . ae day he be flyte wi anither sodger - lad . " Deil hae I ! " quo Tam , for he be a profane swearer . and there be Peden glower at he , gash an waefu ; Peden wi his lang chaft an luntin een , the maud happe about his kist , and the hand of he hold out wi the black nail upon the finger - nebs for he have nae care of the body . " Fy , fy , poor man ! " cry he , " the poor fool man ! Deil hae I , quo he ; an I see the deil at his oxter . " the conviction of guilt and grace cam in on Tam like the deep sea ; he flang doun the pike that be in his hand " I will nae mair lift arm against the cause o Christ ! " say he , and be as gude s word . there be a sair fyke in the beginning , but the governor , see he resolve , gi he his discharge , and he go and dwallt and merried in North Berwick , and have aye a gude name with honest folk free that day on . 

 it be in the year seeventeen hunner and sax that the Bass cam in the hand o the Da rymple , and there be twa man soucht the chairge of it . Baith be weel qualified , for they have baith be sodger in the garrison , and ken the gate to handle solan , and the season and value of they . Forby that they be baith or they baith seem earnest professor and man of comely conversation . the first of they be just Tam Dale , my faither . the second be ane Lapraik , whom the folk can d Tod Lapraik maistly , but whether for his name or his nature I could never hear tell . Weel , Tam gae to see Lapraik upon this business , and take I , that be a toddlin laddie , by the hand . Tod have his dwallin in the lang loan benorth the kirkyaird . it s a dark uncanny loan , forby that the kirk have aye have an ill name since the day o James the Saxt and the deevil s cantrip play therein when the Queen be on the sea ; and as for Tod s house , it be in the mirk end , and be little like by some that ken the good . the door be on the sneck that day , and I and my faither gae straucht in . Tod be a wabster to his trade ; his loom stand in the but . there he sit , a muckle fat , white hash of a man like creish , wi a kind of a holy smile that gart I scunner . the hand of he aye caw the shuttle , but his een be steeke . we cry to he by his name , we skirl in the deid lug of he , we shake he by the shou ther . Nae mainner o service ! there he sit on his dowp , an caw the shuttle and smile like creish . 

 " God be guid to we , " say Tam Dale , " this be no canny ? " 

 he have jimp say the word , when Tod Lapraik cam to himsel . 

 " be this you , Tam ? " say he . " Haith , man ! I m blythe to see ye . I while fa into a bit dwam like this , " he say ; " its frae the stamach . " 

 Weel , they begin to crack about the Bass and which of they twa be to get the warding o t , and little by little cam to very ill word , and twin in anger . I mind weel that as my faither and I gae hame again , he cam ower and ower the same expression , how little he likit Tod Lapraik and his dwam . 

 " Dwam ! " say he . " I think folk hae brunt for dwam like yon . " 

 Aweel , my faither get the Bass and Tod have to go wantin . it be remember sinsyne what way he have ta en the thing . " Tam , " say he , " ye hae get the well o I aince mair , and I hope , " say he , " ye ll find at least a that ye expeckit at the Bass . " which have since be think remarkable expression . at last the time come for Tam Dale to take young solan . this be a business he be weel use wi , he have be a craigsman frae a laddie , and trustit nane but himsel . so there be he hingin by a line an speldering on the craig face , whaur its hie and steigh . fower tenty lad be on the tap , hauldin the line and mindin for his signal . but whaur Tam hang there be naething but the craig , and the sea belaw , and the solan skirlin and fly . it be a braw spring morn , and Tam whustle as he claught in the young geese . Mony s the time I ve hear he tell of this experience , and aye the swat run upon the man . 

 it chance , ye see , that Tam keeke up , and he be awaur of a muckle solan , and the solan pyking at the line . he thocht this by - ordinar and outside the creature s habit . he mind that rope be unco saft thing , and the solan s neb and the Bass Rock unco hard , and that twa hunner foot be raither mair than he would care to fa . 

 " Shoo ! " say Tam . " Awa , bird ! Shoo , awa wi ye ! " say he . 

 the solan keekit doon into Tam s face , and there be something unco in the creature s ee . just the ae keek it gi , and back to the rope . but now it wroucht and warstl t like a thing dementit . there never be the solan make that wroucht as that solan wroucht ; and it seem to understand its employ brawly , birze the saft rope between the neb of it and a crunkle jag o stane . 

 there gae a cauld stend o fear into Tam s heart . " this thing be nae bird , " think he . his een turnt backward in his heid and the day gae black aboot he . " if I get a dwam here , " he toucht , " it s by wi Tam Dale . " and he signal for the lad to pu he up . 

 and it seem the solan understand about signal . for nae soon be the signal make than he let be the rope , sprie his wing , squawk out loud , take a turn fly , and dash straucht at Tam Dale s een . Tam have a knife , he gart the cauld steel glitter . and it seem the solan understand about knife , for nae suner do the steel glint in the sun than he gi the ae squawk , but laighter , like a body disappointit , and flegge aff about the roundness of the craig , and Tam see he nae mair . and as sune as that thing be gane , Tam s heid drapt upon his shouther , and they pu d he up like a deid corp , dadde on the craig . 

 a dram of brandy   which he go never without   broucht he to his mind , or what be leave of it . up he sit . 

 " Rin , Geordie , rin to the boat , mak sure of the boat , man rin ! " he cry , " or yon solan ll have it awa , " say he . 

 the fower lad star at ither , an try to whilly - wha he to be quiet . but naething would satisfy Tam Dale , till ane o they have startit on aheid to stand sentry on the boat . the ither askit if he be for down again . 

 " Na , " say he , " and niether you nor I , " say he , " and as sune as I can win to stand on my twa foot we ll be aff frae this craig o Sawtan . " 

 sure eneuch , nae time be lose , and that be ower muckle ; for before they win to North Berwick Tam be in a cry fever . he lie a the simmer ; and wha be sae kind as come speire for he , but Tod Lapraik ! folk thocht afterwards that ilka time Tod cam near the house the fever have worsen . I kenna for that ; but what I ken the good , that be the end of it . 

 it be about this time o the year ; my grandfaither be out at the white fishing ; and like a bairn , I but to gang wi he . we have a grand take , I mind , and the way that the fish lie broucht we near in by the Bass , whaur we foregaithere wi anither boat that belange to a man Sandie Fletcher in Castleton . he s no lang deid neither , or ye could speir at himsel . Weel , Sandie hail . 

 " what s yon on the Bass ? " say he . 

 " on the Bass ? " say grandfaither . 

 " ay , " say Sandie , " on the green side o t. " 

 " Whatten kind of a thing ? " say grandfaither . " there cannae be naethe on the Bass but just the sheep . " 

 " it look unco like a body , " quo Sandie , who be near in . 

 " a body ! " say we , and we none of we likit that . for there be nae boat that could have bring a man , and the key o the prison yett hung ower my faither s at hame in the press bed . 

 we keept the twa boat close for company , and crap in nearer hand . Grandfaither have a gless , for he have be a sailor , and the captain of a smack , and have lose she on the sand of Tay . and when we take the glass to it , sure eneuch there be a man . he be in a crunkle o green brae , a wee below the chaipel , a by his lee lane , and lowped and flang and dance like a daft quean at a waddin . 

 " it s Tod , " say grandfather , and pass the gless to Sandie . 

 " ay , it s he , " say Sandie . 

 " or ane in the likeness o he , " say grandfaither . 

 " Sma be the differ , " quo Sandie . " De il or warlock , I ll try the gun at he , " quo he , and broucht up a fowling - piece that he aye carry , for Sandie be a notable famous shot in all that country . 

 " haud your hand , Sandie , " say grandfaither ; " we maun see clear first , " say he , " or this may be a dear day s wark to the baith of we . " 

 " Hout ! " say Sandie , " this be the Lord s judgment surely , and be damn to it , " say he . 

 " maybe ay , and maybe no , " say my grandfaither , worthy man ! " but have you a mind of the Procurator Fiscal , that I think ye ll have foregaithere wi before , " say he . 

 this be ower true , and Sandie be a wee thing set ajee . " Aweel , Edie , " say he , " and what would be your way of it ? " 

 " Ou , just this , " say grandfaither . " let I that have the fast boat gang back to North Berwick , and let you bide here and keep an eye on Thon . if I cannae find Lapraik , I ll join ye and the twa of we ll have a crack wi he . but if Lapraik s at hame , I ll rin up the flag at the harbour , and ye can try Thon Thing wi the gun . " 

 Aweel , so it be agree between they twa . I be just a bairn , an clum in Sandie s boat , whaur I thoucht I would see the good of the employ . my grandsire gi Sandie a sill tester to pit in his gun wi the leid drap , bein mair deidly again bogle . and then the as boat set aff for North Berwick , an the tither lie whaur it be and watch the wanchancy thing on the brae - side . 

 a the time we lay there it lowpe and flang and capered and span like a teetotum , and while we could hear it skelloch as it span . I hae see lassie , the daft queans , that would lowp and dance a winter s nicht , and still be lowpe and dance when the winter s day cam in . but there would be fowk there to hauld they company , and the lad to egg they on ; and this thing be its lee - lane . and there would be a fiddler diddle his elbock in the chimney - side ; and this thing have nae music but the skirling of the solan . and the lassie be bit o young thing wi the reid life dinnle and stende in their member ; and this be a muckle , fat , creishy man , and he fa n in the vale o year . say what ye like , I maun say what I believe . it be joy be in the creature s heart , the joy o hell , I daursay : joy whatever . Mony a time I have askit mysel why witch and warlock should sell their saul   whilk be their maist dear possession   and be auld , duddy , wrunkl t wife or auld , feckless , dodder man ; and then I mind upon Tod Lapraik dance a the hour by his lane in the black glory of his heart . Nae doubt they burn for it muckle in hell , but they have a grand time here of it , whatever ! and the Lord forgie we ! 

 Weel , at the hinder end , we see the wee flag yirk up to the mast - heid upon the harbour rock . that be a Sandie wait for . he up wi the gun , take a deleeberate aim , an pu d the trigger . there cam a bang and then ae waefu skirl frae the Bass . and there be we rubbin our een and lookin at ither like daft folk . for wi the bang and the skirl the thing have clean disappear . the sun glintit , the wund blow , and there be the bare yaird whaur the wonder have be lowpe and flinging but ae second syne . 

 the hale way hame I roar and grat wi the terror o that dispensation . the grawn folk be nane sae muckle well ; there be little say in Sandie s boat but just the name of God ; and when we win in by the pier , the harbour rock be fair black wi the folk waitin we . it seem they have fund Lapraik in ane of his dwam , caw the shuttle and smile . ae lad they send to hoist the flag , and the rest abode there in the wabster s house . you may be sure they like it little ; but it be a means of grace to several that stand there pray in to themsel s   for nane care to pray out loud   and look on thon awesome thing as it caw the shuttle . Syne , upon a suddenty , and wi the ae dreidfu skelloch , Tod spring up frae his hinderland and fall forrit on the wab , a bluidy corp . 

 when the corp be examine the leid drap hadnae play buff upon the warlock s body ; sorrow a leid drap be to be fund ! but there be grandfaither s sill tester in the puddock s heart of he . 

 
 Andie have scarce do when there befell a mighty silly affair that have its consequence . Neil , as I have say , be himself a great narrator .  in deal with Highlanders it will be find , and have be show in history , how well it go with Lowland gentlefolk ; but the thing appear scarce feasible for Lowland commons . I have already remark that Andie be continually on the point of quarrel with our three MacGregors , and now , sure enough , it be to come . 

 " Thir will be no word to use to shentleman , " say Neil .

 CHAPTER XVI the missing WITNESS 

 on the seventeenth , the day I be tryste with the Writer , I have much rebellion against fate . the thought of he wait in the King s Arms , and of what he would think , and what he would say when next we meet , torment and oppress I . the truth be unbelievable , so much I have to grant , and it seem cruel hard I should be post as a liar and a coward , and have never consciously omit what it be possible that I should do . I repeat this form of word with a kind of bitter relish , and re - examine in that light the step of my behaviour . it seem I have behave to James Stewart as a brother might ; all the past be a picture that I could be proud of , and there be only the present to consider . I could not swim the sea , nor yet fly in the air , but there be always Andie . "

 early the next morning   Friday , 22nd   a boat come with provision , and Andie place a packet in my hand . the cover be without address but seal with a Government seal . it enclose two note . " Mr. Balfour can now see for himself it be too late to meddle . his conduct will be observe and his discretion reward .  Whereupon , with scarce more word , we step suddenly on board the boat , cast off , and set the lug . the Gregara be then busy upon breakfast , for the cookery be their usual part ; but , one of they step to the battlement , our flight be observe before we be twenty fathom from the rock ; and the three of they run about the ruin and the landing - shelf , for all the world like ant about a broken nest , hail and cry on we to return . we be still in both the lee and the shadow of the rock , which last lie broad upon the water , but presently come forth in almost the same moment into the wind and sunshine ; the sail fill , the boat heel to the gunwale , and we sweep immediately beyond sound of the man s voice . to what terror they endure upon the rock , where they be now desert without the countenance of any civilised person or so much as the protection of a Bible , no limit can be set ; nor have they any brandy leave to be their consolation , for even in the haste and secrecy of our departure Andie have manage to remove it .

 from Duncan I have news of the trial . it be follow in all these Highland region with religious interest ; news of it spread from Inverary as swift as man could travel ; and I be rejoice to learn that , up to a late hour that Saturday it be not yet conclude ; and all man begin to suppose it must spread over the Monday . under the spur of this intelligence I would not sit to eat ; but , Duncan have agree to be my guide , take the road again on foot , with the piece in my hand and munching as I go .  " thirteently , my brother , and in parenthesis , the law itself must be regard as a means of grace , " the minister be say , in the voice of one delight to pursue an argument .

 as for I , I continue to sit there , very wet and weary , and a good deal anxious as to what should happen next , but greatly exult in my success . 

 chapter XVII the MEMORIAL 

 the last word of the blessing be scarce out of the minister s mouth before Stewart have I by the arm . we be the first to be forth of the church , and he make such extraordinary expedition that we be safe within the four wall of a house before the street have begin to be throng with the home - go congregation .

" the case be over ; the jury be enclose , and will so kind as let we ken their view of it to - morrow in the morning , the same as I could have tell it my own self three day ago before the play begin . the thing have be public from the start . the panel ken it , Ye may do what ye will for I , whisper he two day ago . ye ken my fate by what the Duke of Argyle have just say to Mr. Macintosh . o , it s be a scandal !

 James Stewart s counsel be four in number Sheriffs Brown of Colstoun and Miller , Mr. Robert Macintosh , and Mr. Stewart younger of Stewart Hall . these be covenant to dine with the Writer after sermon , and I be very obligingly include of the party . no soon the cloth lift , and the first bowl very artfully compound by Sheriff Miller , than we fall to the subject in hand .  chapter XX I continue to move in good SOCIETY 

 for about exactly two month I remain a guest in Prestongrange s family , where I better my acquaintance with the bench , the bar , and the flower of Edinburgh company . you be not to suppose my education be neglect ; on the contrary , I be keep extremely busy . I study the French , so as to be more prepared to go to Leyden ; I set myself to the fencing , and work hard , sometimes three hour in the day , with notable advancement ; at the suggestion of my cousin , Pilrig , who be an apt musician , I be put to a singing class ; and by the order of my Miss Grant , to one for the dancing , at which I must say I prove far from ornamental . however , all be good enough to say it give I an address a little more genteel ; and there be no question but I learn to manage my coat skirt and sword with more dexterity , and to stand in a room as though the same belong to I . my clothe themselves be all earnestly re - ordered ; and the most trifling circumstance , such as where I should tie my hair , or the colour of my ribbon , debate among the three miss like a thing of weight . one way with another , no doubt I be a good deal improve to look at , and acquire a bit of modest air that would have surprise the good folk at Essendean . 

 the two young miss be very willing to discuss a point of my habiliment , because that be in the line of their chief thought . I can not say that they appear any other way conscious of my presence ; and though always more than civil , with a kind of heartless cordiality , could not hide how much I weary they . as for the aunt , she be a wonderful still woman ; and I think she give I much the same attention as she give the rest of the family , which be little enough . the eld daughter and the Advocate himself be thus my principal friend , and our familiarity be much increase by a pleasure that we take in common . before the court meet we spend a day or two at the house of Grange , live very nobly with an open table , and here it be that we three begin to ride out together in the field , a practice afterwards maintain in Edinburgh , so far as the Advocate s continual affair permit . when we be put in a good frame by the briskness of the exercise , the difficulty of the way , or the accident of bad weather , my shyness wear entirely off ; we forget that we be stranger , and speech not be require , it flow the more naturally on . then it be that they have my story from I , bit by bit , from the time that I leave Essendean , with my voyage and battle in the Covenant , wandering in the heather , etc . ; and from the interest they find in my adventure spring the circumstance of a jaunt we make a little later on , on a day when the court be not sit , and of which I will tell a trifle more at length . 

 we take horse early , and pass first by the house of Shaws , where it stand smokeless in a great field of white frost , for it be yet early in the day . here Prestongrange alight down , give I his horse , an proceeded alone to visit my uncle . my heart , I remember , swell up bitter within I at the sight of that bare house and the thought of the old miser sitting chitter within in the cold kitchen !

Prestongrange and his grace the Lord President may have hear of it   for what I know   on the deaf side of their head ; they keep it to themselves , at least the public be none the wiser ; and in course of time , on November 8th , and in the midst of a prodigious storm of wind and rain , poor James of the Glens be duly hang at Lettermore by Ballachulish . 

 so there be the final upshot of my politic ! innocent man have perish before James , and be like to keep on perish   in spite of all our wisdom   till the end of time . and till the end of time young folk   who be not yet use with the duplicity of life and man   will struggle as I do , and make heroical resolve , and take long risk ; and the course of event will push they upon the one side and go on like a march army . James be hang ; and here be I dwell in the house of Prestongrange , and grateful to he for his fatherly attention . he be hang ; and behold ! when I meet Mr. Simon in the causeway , I be fain to pull off my beaver to he like a good little boy before his dominie . he have be hang by fraud and violence , and the world wag along , and there be not a pennyweight of difference ; and the villain of that horrid plot be decent , kind , respectable father of family , who go to kirk and take the sacrament ! 

 but I have have my view of that detestable business they call politic I have see it from behind , when it be all bone and blackness ; and I be cure for life of any temptation to take part in it again . a plain , quiet , private path be that which I be ambitious to walk in , when I might keep my head out of the way of danger and my conscience out of the road of temptation . for , upon a retrospect , it appear I have not do so grandly , after all ; but with the great possible amount of big speech and preparation , have accomplish nothing . 

 the 25th of the same month a ship be advertise to sail from Leith ; and I be suddenly recommend to make up my mail for Leyden . to Prestongrange I could , of course , say nothing ; for I have already be a long while sorne on his house and table . but with his daughter I be more open , bewail my fate that I should be send out of the country , and assure she , unless she should bring I to farewell with Catriona , I would refuse at the last hour . 

 " have I not give you my advice ? " she ask . 

 " I know you have , " say I , " and I know how much I be beholden to you already , and that I be bid to obey your order . but you must confess you be something too merry a lass at time to lippen   23   to entirely . "

I know she consider I too backward , and rather desire to rise in her opinion on that head . besides which , after so much affection show and   I believe   feel upon both side , it would have look cold - like to be anyways stiff . accordingly , I get my courage up and my word ready , and the last chance we be like to be alone , ask pretty boldly to be allow to salute she in farewell .

" do you think that I would let we part like stranger ? because I can never keep my gravity at you five minute on end , you must not dream I do not love you very well : I be all love and laughter , every time I cast an eye on you ! and now I will give you an advice to conclude your education , which you will have need of before it s very long . never ask womenfolk . they re bind to answer no ; God never make the lass that could resist the temptation . it s suppose by divine to be the curse of Eve : because she do not say it when the devil offer she the apple , her daughter can say nothing else . " 

 " since I be so soon to lose my bonny professor , " I begin . 

 " this be gallant , indeed , " say she curtsey . 

 " I would put the one question , " I go on . " may I ask a lass to marry to I ? " 

 " you think you could not marry she without ! " she ask . " or else get she to offer ? " 

 " you see you can not be serious , " say I. 

 " I shall be very serious in one thing , David , " say she : " I shall always be your friend . " 

 as I get to my horse the next morning , the four lady be all at that same window whence we have once look down on Catriona , and all cry farewell and wave their pocket napkin as I ride away . one out of the four I know be truly sorry ; and at the thought of that , and how I have come to the door three month ago for the first time , sorrow and gratitude make a confusion in my mind . 

 PART ii FATHER and DAUGHTER 

 CHAPTER XXI the VOYAGE into HOLLAND 

 the ship lie at a single anchor , well outside the pier of Leith , so that all we passenger must come to it by the mean of skiff . this be very little troublesome , for the reason that the day be a flat calm , very frosty and cloudy , and with a low shift fog upon the water . the body of the vessel be thus quite hide as I draw near , but the tall spar of she stand high and bright in a sunshine like the flickering of a fire . she prove to be a very roomy , commodious merchant , but somewhat blunt in the bow , and loaden extraordinary deep with salt , salt salmon , and fine white linen stocking for the Dutch . upon my come on board , the captain welcome I one Sang   out of Lesmahago , I believe , a very hearty , friendly tarpaulin of a man , but at the moment in rather of a bustle . there have no other of the passenger yet appear , so that I be leave to walk about upon the deck , view the prospect and wonder a good deal what these farewell should be which I be promise .

 CHAPTER XXII HELVOETSLUYS 

 the weather in the end considerably worsen ; the wind sing in the shroud , the sea swell higher , and the ship begin to labour and cry out among the billow . the song of the leadsman in the chain be now scarce cease , for we thrid all the way among shoal . about nine in the morning , in a burst of wintry sun between two squall of hail , I have my first look of Holland a line of windmill birl in the breeze . it be besides my first knowledge of these daft - like contrivance , which give I a near sense of foreign travel and a new world and life . we come to an anchor about half - past eleven , outside the harbour of Helvoetsluys , in a place where the sea sometimes break and the ship pitch outrageously . you may be sure we be all on deck save Mrs. Gebbie , some of we in cloak , other mantle in the ship s tarpaulin , all cling on by rope , and jest the most like old sailor - folk that we could imitate . 

 presently a boat , that be back like a partancrab , come gingerly alongside , and the skipper of it hail our master in the Dutch . Thence Captain Sang turn , very trouble - like , to Catriona ; and the rest of we crowd about , the nature of the difficulty be make plain to all . the Rose be bind to the port of Rotterdam , whither the other passenger be in a great impatience to arrive , in view of a conveyance due to leave that very evening in the direction of the Upper Germany . this , with the present half - gale of wind , the captain   if no time be lose   declare himself still capable to save . now James More have tryste in Helvoet with his daughter , and the captain have engage to call before the port and place she   accord to the custom   in a shore boat . there be the boat , to be sure , and here be Catriona ready : but both our master and the patroon of the boat scruple at the risk , and the first be in no humour to delay . 

 " your father , " say he , " would be gey an little pleased if we be to break a leg to ye , Miss Drummond , let - a - be drown of you . take my way of it , " say he , " and come on - by with the rest of we here to Rotterdam . Ye can get a passage down the Maes in a sailing scoot as far as to the Brill , and thence on again , by a place in a rattel - waggon , back to Helvoet . " 

 but Catriona would hear of no change . she look white - like as she behold the bursting of the spray , the green sea that sometimes pour upon the fore - castle , and the perpetual bounding and swooping of the boat among the billow ; but she stand firmly by her father s order . " my father , James More , will have arrange it so , " be her first word and her last . I think it very idle and indeed wanton in the girl to be so literal and stand opposite to so much kind advice ; but the fact be she have a very good reason , if she would have tell we . sailing scoot and rattel - waggon be excellent thing ; only the use of they must first be pay for , and all she be possess of in the world be just two shilling and a penny halfpenny sterling . so it fall out that captain and passenger , not know of her destitution and she be too proud to tell they speak in vain . 

 " but you ken nae French and nae Dutch neither , " say one . 

 " it be very true , " say she , " but since the year 46 there be so many of the honest Scotch abroad that I will be do very well . I thank you . " 

 there be a pretty country simplicity in this that make some laugh , other look the more sorry , and Mr. Gebbie fall outright in a passion . I believe he know it be his duty   his wife have accept charge of the girl   to have go ashore with she and see she safe : nothing would have induce he to have do so , since it must have involve the lose of his conveyance ; and I think he make it up to his conscience by the loudness of his voice . at least he break out upon Captain Sang , rag and say the thing be a disgrace ; that it be mere death to try to leave the ship , and at any event we could not cast down an innocent maid in a boatful of nasty Holland fisher , and leave she to her fate . I be think something of the same ; take the mate upon one side , arrange with he to send on my chest by track - scoot to an address I have in Leyden , and stand up and signal to the fisher . 

 " I will go ashore with the young lady , Captain Sang , " say i. " it be all one what way I go to Leyden ; " and leap at the same time into the boat , which I manage not so elegantly but what I fall with two of the fisher in the bilge . 

 from the boat the business appear yet more precarious than from the ship , she stand so high over we , swing down so swift , and menace we so perpetually with she plunge and passage upon the anchor cable . I begin to think I have make a fool s bargain , that it be merely impossible Catriona should be get on board to I , and that I stand to be set ashore at Helvoet all by myself and with no hope of any reward but the pleasure of embrace James More , if I should want to . but this be to reckon without the lass s courage . she have see I leap with very little appearance   however much reality   of hesitation ; to be sure , she be not to be beat by her discard friend . up she stand on the bulwark and hold by a stay , the wind blow in her petticoat , which make the enterprise more dangerous , and give we rather more of a view of her stocking than would be think genteel in city . there be no minute lose , and scarce time give for any to interfere if they have wish the same . I stand up on the other side and spread my arm ; the ship swing down on we , the patroon humour his boat nearer in than be perhaps wholly safe , and Catriona leap into the air . I be so happy as to catch she , and the fisher readily support we , escape a fall . she hold to I a moment very tight , breathe quick and deep ; thence   she still cling to I with both hand   we be pass aft to our place by the steersman ; and Captain Sang and all the crew and passenger cheer and cry farewell , the boat be put about for shore . 

 as soon as Catriona come a little to herself she unhand I suddenly , but say no word . no more do I ; and indeed the whistling of the wind and the breaching of the spray make it no time for speech ; and our crew not only toil excessively but make extremely little way , so that the Rose have get her anchor and be off again before we have approach the harbour mouth . 

 we be no soon in smooth water than the patroon , accord to their beastly holland custom , stop his boat and require of we our fare . two guilde be the man s demand between three and four shilling english money for each passenger . but at this Catriona begin to cry out with a vast deal of agitation . she have ask of Captain Sang , she say , and the fare be but an English shilling . " cry she . the patroon scold back upon she in a lingo where the oath be English and the rest right holland ; till at last   see she near tear   I privately slip in the rogue s hand six shilling , whereupon he be oblige enough to receive from she the other shilling without more complaint . no doubt I be a good deal nettled and ashamed . I like to see folk thrifty , but not with so much passion ; and I daresay it would be rather coldly that I ask she , as the boat move on again for shore , where it be that she be tryste with her father .

 " it will be time enough when I get you to your father , " say I , little thinking that I speak so true . " I can tell he a fine tale of a loyal daughter . " 

 " o , I do not think I will be a loyal girl , at all event , " she cry , with a great deal of painfulness in the expression . " I do not think my heart be true . " 

 " yet there be very few that would have make that leap , and all to obey a father s order , " I observe . 

 " I can not have you to be think of I so , " she cry again . " when you have do that same , how would I stop behind ? and at all event that be not all the reason . " Whereupon , with a burn face , she tell I the plain truth upon her poverty . 

 " good guide we ! " cry I , " what kind of daft - like proceeding be this , to let yourself be launch on the continent of Europe with an empty purse I count it hardly decent scant decent ! " I cry . 

 " you forget James More , my father , be a poor gentleman , " say she . " he be a hunted exile . " 

 " but I think not all your friend be hunt exile , " I exclaim . " and be this fair to they that care for you ? be it fair to I ? be it fair to Miss Grant that counsel you to go , and would be drive fair horn - mad if she could hear of it ? be it even fair to these Gregory folk that you be live with , and use you lovingly ? it s a blessing you have fall in my hand ! suppose your father hinder by an accident , what would become of you here , and you your lee - lone in a strange place ? the thought of the thing frighten I , " I say . 

 " I will have lie to all of they , " she reply . " I will have tell they all that I have plenty . I tell she too . I could not be lower James More to they . " 

 I find out later on that she must have lower he in the very dust , for the lie be originally the father s , not the daughter s , and she thus oblige to persevere in it for the man s reputation . but at the time I be ignorant of this , and the mere thought of her destitution and the peril in which see must have fall , have ruffle I almost beyond reason . 

 " well , well , well , " say I , " you will have to learn more sense . " 

 I leave her mail for the moment in an inn upon the shore , where I get a direction for Sprott s house in my new French , and we walk there it be some little way behold the place with wonder as we go . indeed , there be much for scot folk to admire : canal and tree be intermingle with the house ; the house , each within itself , of a brave red brick , the colour of a rose , with step and bench of blue marble at the cheek of every door , and the whole town so clean you might have din upon the causeway . Sprott be within , upon his ledger , in a low parlour , very neat and clean , and set out with china and picture , and a globe of the earth in a brass frame . he be a big - chafted , ruddy , lusty man , with a crooked hard look to he ; and he make we not that much civility as offer we a seat . 

 " be James More Macgregor now in Helvoet , sir ? " say I. 

 " I ken nobody by such a name , " say he , impatient - like . 

 " since you be so particular , " say I , " I will amend my question , and ask you where we be to find in Helvoet one James Drummond , alias Macgregor , alia James More , late tenant in inveronachile ? " 

 " Sir , " say he , " he may be in Hell for what I ken , and for my part I wish he be . " 

 " the young lady be that gentleman s daughter , sir , " say I , " before whom , I think you will agree with I , it be not very become to discuss his character . " 

 " I have nothing to make either with he , or she , or you ! " cry he in his gross voice . 

 " under your favour , Mr. Sprott , " say I , " this young lady be come from Scotland seek he , and by whatever mistake , be give the name of your house for a direction . an error it seem to have be , but I think this place both you and I who be but her fellow - traveller by accident under a strong obligation to help our countrywoman . " 

 " will you de I daft ? " he cry . " I tell ye I ken naething and care less either for he or his breed . I tell ye the man owe I money . " 

 " that may very well be , sir , " say I , who be now rather more angry than himself . " at least , I owe you nothing ; the young lady be under my protection ; and I be neither at all use with these manner , nor in the least content with they . " 

 as I say this , and without particularly think what I do , I draw a step or two nearer to his table ; thus strike , by mere good fortune , on the only argument that could at all affect the man . the blood leave his lusty countenance . 

 " for the Lord s sake dinna be hasty , sir ! " he cry . " I be truly wishfu no to be offensive . but ye ken , sir , I m like a wheen guid - nature , honest , canty auld fellow my bark be waur nor my bite . to hear I , ye micht while fancy I be a wee thing dour ; but na , na ! it s a kind auld fallow at heart , Sandie Sprott ! and ye could never imagine the fyke and fash this man have be to I . " 

 " very good , sir , " say I. " then I will make that much freedom with your kindness as trouble you for your last news of Mr. Drummond . " 

 " you re welcome , sir ! " say he . " as for the young leddy   my respect to she ! , he ll just have clean forget she . I ken the man , ye see ; I have lose siller by he ere now . he think of naebody but just himsel ; clan , king , or dauchter , if he can get his wameful , he would give they a the go - by ! ay , or his correspondent either . for there be a sense in whilk I may be nearly almost say to be his correspondent . the fact be , we be employ thegether in a business affair , and I think it s like to turn out a dear affair for Sandie Sprott . the man s as guid s my pairtner , and I give ye my mere word I ken naethe by where he be . he micht be come here to Helvoet ; he micht come here the morn , he michtnae come for a twalmouth ; I would wonder at naethe or just at the ae thing , and that s if he be to pay I my siller . ye see what way I stand with it ; and it s clear I m no very likely to meddle up with the young leddy , as ye can she . she cannae stop here , that s ae thing certain sure . Dod , sir , I m a lone man ! if I be to tak she in , its highly possible the hellicat would try and gar I marry she when he turn up . " 

 " enough of this talk , " say I. " I will take the young leddy among well friend . give I , pen , ink , and paper , and I will leave here for James More the address of my correspondent in Leyden . he can inquire from I where he be to seek his daughter . " 

 this word I write and seal ; which while I be do , Sprott of his own motion make a welcome offer , to charge himself with Miss Drummond s mail , and even send a porter for they to the inn . I advance he to that effect a dollar or two to be a cover , and he give I an acknowledgment in writing of the sum . 

 Whereupon   I give my arm to Catriona   we leave the house of this unpalatable rascal . she have say no word throughout , leave I to judge and speak in her place ; I , upon my side , have be careful not to embarrass she by a glance ; and even now , although my heart still glow inside of I with shame and anger , I make it my affair to seem quite easy . 

 " now , " say I , " let we get back to yon same inn where they can speak the French , have a piece of dinner , and inquire for conveyance to Rotterdam . I will never be easy till I have you safe again in the hand of Mrs. Gebbie . " 

 " I suppose it will have to be , " say Catriona , " though whoever will be please , I do not think it will be she . and I will remind you this once again that I have but one shilling , and three baubee . " 

 " and just this once again , " say I , " I will remind you it be a blessing that I come alongst with you . " 

 " what else would I be think all this time ? " say she , and I think weigh a little on my arm . " it be you that be the good friend to I . " 

 CHAPTER XXIII travel in HOLLAND 

 the rattel - waggon , which be a kind of a long waggon set with bench , carry we in four hour of travel to the great city of Rotterdam . it be long past dark by then , but the street be pretty brightly light and throng with wild - like , outlandish character beard Hebrews , black man , and the horde of courtesans , most indecently adorn with finery and stop seaman by their very sleeve ; the clash of talk about we make our head to whirl ; and what be the most unexpected of all , we appear to be no more strike with all these foreigner than they with we . I make the good face I could , for the lass s sake and my own credit ; but the truth be I feel like a lost sheep , and my heart beat in my bosom with anxiety . once or twice I inquire after the harbour or the berth of the ship Rose : but either fall on some who speak only holland , or my own French fail I . try a street at a venture , I come upon a lane of lighted house , the door and window throng with wauf - like paint woman ; these jostle and mock upon we as we pass , and I be thankful we have nothing of their language . a little after we issue forth upon an open place along the harbour . 

 " we shall be do now , " cry I , as soon as I spy mast . " let we walk here by the harbour . we be sure to meet some that have the English , and at the good of it we may light upon that very ship . " 

 we do the next good , as happen ; for , about nine of the evening , whom should we walk into the arm of but Captain Sang ? he tell we they have make their run in the most incredible brief time , the wind hold strong till they reach port ; by which mean his passenger be all go already on their further travel . it be impossible to chase after the gebbie into the High Germany , and we have no other acquaintance to fall back upon but Captain sing himself . it be the more gratifying to find the man friendly and wishful to assist . he make it a small affair to find some good plain family of merchant , where Catriona might harbour till the Rose be loaden ; declare he would then blithely carry she back to Leith for nothing and see she safe in the hand of Mr. Gregory ; and in the meanwhile carry we to a late ordinary for the meal we stand in need of . he seem extremely friendly , as I say , but what surprise I a good deal , rather boisterous in the bargain ; and the cause of this be soon to appear . for at the ordinary , call for Rhenish wine and drinking of it deep , he soon become unutterably tipsy . in this case , as too common with all man , but especially with those of his rough trade , what little sense or manner he possess desert he ; and he behave himself so scandalous to the young lady , jest most ill - favouredly at the figure she have make on the ship s rail , that I have no resource but carry she suddenly away . 

 she come out of the ordinary clinging to I close . " take I away , David , " she say . " you keep I . I be not afraid with you . " 

 " and have no cause , my little friend ! " cry I , and could have find it in my heart to weep . 

 " where will you be take I ? " she say again . " Don t leave I at all event never leave I . " 

 " where be I take you to ? " say I stop , for I have be stave on ahead in mere blindness . " I must stop and think . but I ll not leave you , Catriona ; the Lord do so to I , and more also , if I should fail or fash you . " 

 she creep close into I by way of a reply . 

 " here , " I say , " be the still place we have hit on yet in this busy byke of a city . let we sit down here under yon tree and consider of our course . " 

 that tree   which I be little like to forget   stand hard by the harbour side . it be like a black night , but light be in the house , and near hand in the quiet ship ; there be a shining of the city on the one hand , and a buzz hang over it of many thousand walk and talk ; on the other , it be dark and the water bubble on the side . I spread my cloak upon a builder s stone , and make she sit there ; she would have keep she hold upon I , for she still shake with the late affront ; but I want to think clear , disengage myself , and pace to and fro before she , in the manner of what we call a smuggler s walk , belabour my brain for any remedy . by the course of these scatter thought I be bring suddenly face to face with a remembrance that , in the heat and haste of our departure , I have leave Captain Sang to pay the ordinary . at this I begin to laugh out loud , for I think the man well serve ; and at the same time , by an instinctive movement , carry my hand to the pocket where my money be . I suppose it be in the lane where the woman jostle we ; but there be only the one thing certain , that my purse be go . 

 " you will have think of something good , " say she , observe I to pause . 

 at the pinch we be in , my mind become suddenly clear as a perspective glass , and I see there be no choice of method . I have not one doit of coin , but in my pocket - book I have still my letter on the Leyden merchant ; and there be now but the one way to get to Leyden , and that be to walk on our two foot . 

 " Catriona , " say I , " I know you re brave and I believe you re strong do you think you could walk thirty mile on a plain road ? " we find it , I believe , scarce the two - third of that , but such be my notion of the distance . 

 " David , " she say , " if you will just keep near , I will go anywhere and do anything . the courage of my heart , it be all break . do not be leave I in this horrible country by myself , and I will do all else . " 

 " can you start now and march all night ? " say I. 

 " I will do all that you can ask of I , " she say , " and never ask you why . I have be a bad ungrateful girl to you ; and do what you please with I now ! and I think Miss Barbara Grant be the good lady in the world , " she add , " and I do not see what she would deny you for at all event . " 

 this be greek and Hebrew to I ; but I have other matter to consider , and the first of these be to get clear of that city on the Leyden road . it prove a cruel problem ; and it may have be one or two at night ere we have solve it . once beyond the house , there be neither moon nor star to guide we ; only the whiteness of the way in the midst and a blackness of an alley on both hand . the walking be besides make most extraordinary difficult by a plain black frost that fall suddenly in the small hour and turn that highway into one long slide . 

 " well , Catriona , " say I , " here we be like the king s son and the old wife daughter in your daft - like Highland tale . soon we ll be go over the seven ben , the seven glen and the seven mountain moor . " which be a common byword or overcome in those tale of hers that have stick in my memory .

 " I will never complain of the country of my friend , " say she , and speak it out with an accent so particular that I seem to see the look upon her face . 

 I catch in my breath sharp and come near fall   for my pain   on the black ice .

 " it be a good day when you show I so much love , " say she . 

 " and yet I think shame to be happy too , " I go on , " and you here on the road in the black night . " 

 " where in the great world would I be else ? " she cry . " I be think I be safest where I be with you . " 

 " I be quite forgive , then ? " I ask .

 " be this Miss Grant again ? " say I. " you say yourself she be the good lady in the world . "

 " well , " say I , " this beat all that ever come to my knowledge ; and I wonder that you can indulge yourself in such bairnly whim . here be a young lady that be the good friend in the world to the both of we , that learn we how to dress ourselves , and in a great manner how to behave , as anyone can see that know we both before and after . " 

 but Catriona stop square in the midst of the highway . 

 " it be this way of it , " say she . " either you will go on to speak of she , and I will go back to yon town , and let come of it what God please ! or else you will do I that politeness to talk of other thing . " 

 I be the most nonplussed person in this world ; but I bethink I that she depend altogether on my help , that she be of the frail sex and not so much beyond a child , and it be for I to be wise for the pair of we . 

 " my dear girl , " say I , " I can make neither head nor tail of this ; but God forbid that I should do anything to set you on the jee . as for talk of Miss Grant , I have no such a mind to it , and I believe it be yourself begin it . my only design   if I take you up at all   be for your own improvement , for I hate the very look of injustice . not that I do not wish you to have a good pride and a nice female delicacy ; they become you well ; but here you show they to excess . " 

 " well , then , have you do ? " say she . 

 " I have do , " say I. 

 " a very good thing , " say she , and we go on again , but now in silence . 

 it be an eerie employment to walk in the gross night , behold only shadow and hear nought but our own step . at first , I believe our heart burn against each other with a deal of enmity ; but the darkness and the cold , and the silence , which only the cock sometimes interrupt , or sometimes the farmyard dog , have pretty soon bring down our pride to the dust ; and for my own particular , I would have jump at any decent opening for speech . 

 before the day peep , come on a warmish rain , and the frost be all wipe away from among our foot . I take my cloak to she and seek to hap she in the same ; she bid I , rather impatiently , to keep it . 

 " indeed and I will do no such thing , " say I. " here be I , a great , ugly lad that have see all kind of weather , and here be you a tender , pretty maid ! my dear , you would not put I to a shame ? " 

 without more word she let I cover she ; which as I be do in the darkness , I let my hand rest a moment on her shoulder , almost like an embrace . 

 " you must try to be more patient of your friend , " say I. 

 I think she seem to lean the least thing in the world against my bosom , or perhaps it be but fancy . 

 " there will be no end to your goodness , " say she . 

 and we go on again in silence ; but now all be change ; and the happiness that be in my heart be like a fire in a great chimney . 

 the rain pass ere day ; it be but a sloppy morning as we come into the town of Delft . the red gable house make a handsome show on either hand of a canal ; the servant lassie be out slestere and scrub at the very stone upon the public highway ; smoke rise from a hundred kitchen ; and it come in upon I strongly it be time to break our fast . 

 " Catriona , " say I , " I believe you have yet a shilling and three baubee ? " 

 " be you want it ? " say she , and pass I her purse . " I be wish it be five pound ! what will you want it for ? " 

 " and what have we be walk for all night , like a pair of waif Egyptians ! " say I. " just because I be rob of my purse and all I possess in that unchancy town of Rotterdam . I will tell you of it now , because I think the bad be over , but we have still a good tramp before we till we get to where my money be , and if you would not buy I a piece of bread , I be like to go fast . " 

 she look at I with open eye . by the light of the new day she be all black and pale for weariness , so that my heart smite I for she . but as for she , she break out laugh . 

 " my torture ! be we beggar then ! " she cry . " you too ? o , I could have wish for this same thing ! and I be glad to buy your breakfast to you . but it would be pleisand if I would have have to dance to get a meal to you ! for I believe they be not very well acquainted with our manner of dance over here , and might be pay for the curiosity of that sight . " 

 I could have kiss she for that word , not with a lover s mind , but in a heat of admiration . for it always warm a man to see a woman brave . 

 we get a drink of milk from a country wife but new come to the town , and in a baker s , a piece of excellent , hot , sweet - smell bread , which we eat upon the road as we go on . that road from Delft to the Hague be just five mile of a fine avenue shade with tree , a canal on the one hand , on the other excellent pasture of cattle . it be pleasant here indeed . 

 " and now , Davie , " say she , " what will you do with I at all event ? " 

 " it be what we have to speak of , " say I , " and the soon yet the well . I can come by money in Leyden ; that will be all well . but the trouble be how to dispose of you until your father come . I think last night you seem a little sweir to part from I ? "

 " and now I will be Catriona Balfour , " she say . " and who be to ken ? they be all strange folk here . "

 " I will have no choice leave , " say she . " my father James More have not use I very well , and it be not the first time , I be cast upon your hand like a sack of barley meal , and have nothing else to think of but your pleasure . if you will have I , good and well . if you will not " she turn and touch her hand upon my arm " David , I be afraid , " say she . 

 " no , but I ought to warn you , " I begin ; and then bethink I I be the bearer of the purse , and it would never do to seem too churlish . " Catriona , " say I , " don t misunderstand I : I be just try to do my duty by you , girl ! here be I go alone to this strange city , to be a solitary student there ; and here be this chance arise that you might dwell with I a bit , and be like my sister ; you can surely understand this much , my dear , that I would just love to have you ? "

I know this be a great blot on my character , for which I be lucky that I do not pay more dear . but I mind how easy her delicacy have be startle with a word of kiss she in Barbara s letter ; now that she depend on I , how be I to be more bold ? besides , the truth be , I could see no other feasible method to dispose of she . and I daresay inclination pull I very strong .

I could see my Dutchman be extremely suspicious ; and view I over the rim of a great pair of spectacle he be a poor , frail body , and remind I of an infirm rabbit he begin to question I close .

I shall have a fine ravel pirn to unwind , and may end by disgrace both the lassie and myself . thereupon I begin hastily to expound to he my sister s character . she be of a bashful disposition , it appear , and be extremely fearful of meet stranger that I have leave she at that moment sit in a public place alone . and then , be launch upon the stream of falsehood , I must do like all the rest of the world in the same circumstance , and plunge in deep than be any service ; add some altogether needless particular of Miss Balfour s ill - health and retirement during childhood . in the midst of which I awake to a sense of my behaviour , and be turn to one blush . 

 the old gentleman be not so much deceive but what he discover a willingness to be quit of I . but he be first of all a man of business ; and know that my money be good enough , however it might be with my conduct , he be so far oblige as to send his son to be my guide and caution in the matter of a lodging . this imply my presenting of the young man to Catriona . the poor , pretty child be much recover with resting , look and behave to perfection , and take my arm and give I the name of brother more easily than I could answer she . but there be one misfortune : think to help , she be rather towardly than otherwise to my Dutchman . and I could not but reflect that Miss Balfour have rather suddenly outgrown her bashfulness . and there be another thing , the difference of our speech . I have the Low Country tongue and dwell upon my word ; she have a hill voice , speak with something of an English accent , only far more delightful , and be scarce quite fit to be call a deacon in the craft of talk English grammar ; so that , for a brother and sister , we make a most uneven pair . but the young Hollander be a heavy dog , without so much spirit in his belly as to remark her prettiness , for which I scorn he . and as soon as he have find a cover to our head , he leave we alone , which be the great service of the two . 

 CHAPTER XXIV FULL story of a copy of heinecciu 

 the place find be in the upper part of a house back on a canal . we have two room , the second enter from the first ; each have a chimney build out into the floor in the dutch manner ; and be alongside , each have the same prospect from the window of the top of a tree below we in a little court , of a piece of the canal , and of house in the holland architecture and a church spire upon the further side . a full set of bell hang in that spire and make delightful music ; and when there be any sun at all , it shine direct in our two chamber . from a tavern hard by we have good meal send in .

 CHAPTER XXV the return of JAMES MORE 

 I be call on the morrow out of a late and troubled slumber by a knocking on my door , run to open it , and have almost swoon with the contrariety of my feeling , mostly painful ; for on the threshold , in a rough wraprascal and an extraordinary big laced hat , there stand James More .

 CHAPTER XXVI the THREESOME 

 whether or not I be to be so much blame , or rather perhaps pity , I must leave other to judge . my shrewdness   of which I have a good deal , too   seem not so great with the lady . no doubt , at the moment when I awake she , I be think a good deal of the effect upon James More ; and similarly when I return and we be all sit down to breakfast , I continue to behave to the young lady with deference and distance ; as I still think to have be most wise . her father have cast doubt upon the innocence of my friendship ; and these , it be my first business to allay . but there be a kind of an excuse for Catriona also . we have share in a scene of some tenderness and passion , and give and receive caress : I have thrust she from I with violence ; I have call aloud upon she in the night from the one room to the other ; she have pass hour of wakefulness and weeping ; and it be not to be suppose I have be absent from her pillow thought . upon the back of this , to be awake , with unaccustomed formality , under the name of Miss Drummond , and to be thenceforth use with a great deal of distance and respect , lead she entirely in error on my private sentiment ; and she be indeed so incredibly abuse as to imagine I repentant and try to draw off !

 chapter XXVII a TWOSOME

 CHAPTER XXVIII in which I be left alone

 CHAPTER XXIX we meet in DUNKIRK

 CHAPTER XXX the letter from the SHIP 

 Daylight show we how solitary the inn stand . it be plainly hard upon the sea , yet out of all view of it , and beset on every side with scabbit hill of sand . there be , indeed , only one thing in the nature of a prospect , where there stand out over a brae the two sail of a windmill , like an ass s ear , but with the ass quite hide . it be strange   after the wind rise , for at first it be dead calm   to see the turning and following of each other of these great sail behind the hillock . Scarce any road come by there ; but a number of footway travel among the bent in all direction up to Mr. Bazin s door . the truth be , he be a man of many trade , not any one of they honest , and the position of his inn be the good of his livelihood . smuggler frequent it ; political agent and forfeit person bind across the water come there to await their passage ; and I daresay there be bad behind , for a whole family might have be butcher in that house and nobody the wiser . 

 I sleep little and ill . long ere it be day , I have slip from beside my bedfellow , and be warm myself at the fire or walk to and fro before the door . Dawn break mighty sullen ; but a little after , spring up a wind out of the west , which burst the cloud , let through the sun , and set the mill to the turning . there be something of spring in the sunshine , or else it be in my heart ; and the appearing of the great sail one after another from behind the hill , divert I extremely . at time I could hear a creak of the machinery ; and by half - past eight of the day , and I think this dreary , desert place be like a paradise . 

 for all which , as the day draw on and nobody come near , I begin to be aware of an uneasiness that I could scarce explain . it seem there be trouble afoot ; the sail of the windmill , as they come up and go down over the hill , be like person spy ; and outside of all fancy , it be surely a strange neighbourhood and house for a young lady to be bring to dwell in . 

 at breakfast , which we take late , it be manifest that James More be in some danger or perplexity ; manifest that Alan be alive to the same , and watch he close ; and this appearance of duplicity upon the one side , and vigilance upon the other , hold I on live coal . the meal be no soon over than James seem to come begin to make apology . he have an appointment of a private nature in the town   it be with the french nobleman , he tell I , and we would please excuse he till about noon . meanwhile he carry his daughter aside to the far end of the room , where he seem to speak rather earnestly and she to listen with much inclination . 

 " I be care less and less about this man James , " say Alan . " there s something no right with the man James , and I shouldnae wonder but what Alan Breck would give an eye to he this day . I would like fine to see yon french nobleman , Davie ; and I daresay you could find an employ to yoursel , and that would be to speir at the lassie for some news o your affair . just tell it to she plainly tell she ye re a muckle ass at the off - set ; and then , if I be you , and ye could do it naitural , I would just mint to she I be in some kind of a danger ; a weemenfolk like that . " 

 " I cannae lee , Alan , I cannae do it naitural , " say I , mock he . 

 " the more fool you ! " say he . " then ye ll can tell she that I recommend it ; that ll set she to the laughing ; and I wouldnae wonder but what that be the next good . but see to the pair of they ! if I didnae feel just sure of the lassie , and that she be awful pleased and chief with Alan , I would think there be some kind of hocus - pocus about you . " 

 " and be she so pleased with ye , then , Alan ? " I ask .

 he come with one of his queer smile . " what be I tell ye , David ? " say he .

 " ay , but I would never trust Alan whether he be asleep or wake ! " say he . " but the business look bad . let s see the letter . " 

 I give it he .

 " it be my wish , " say Catriona . 

 he open it , glance it through , and fling his hand in the air .

 the way that he be follow bring we close in by the windmill , where I be aware of a man in seaman s trouser , who seem to be spy from behind it . only , of course , we take he in the rear . 

 " see , Alan ! " 

 " Wheesht ! " say , he , " this be my affair . "
