 as soon as we appear , they cast off all disguise upon the other side ; and the seaman pursue we with shout and view - hullohs . we have a start of some two hundred yard , and they be but bandy - legged tarpaulin after all , that could not hope to better we at such an exercise . I suppose they be arm , but do not care to use their pistol on french ground . and as soon as I perceive that we not only hold our advantage but draw a little away , I begin to feel quite easy of the issue . for all which , it be a hot , brisk bit of work , so long as it last ; Dunkirk be still far off ; and when we pop over a knowe , and find a company of the garrison marching on the other side on some manouvre , I could very well understand the word that Alan have . 

 he stop run at once ; and mop at his brow , " they re a real bonny folk , the french nation , " say he . 

 conclusion 

 no soon be we safe within the wall of Dunkirk than we hold a very necessary council - of - war on our position . we have take a daughter from her father at the sword s point ; any judge would give she back to he at once , and by all likelihood clap I and Alan into jail ; and though we have an argument upon our side in Captain Palliser s letter , neither Catriona nor I be very keen to be use it in public . upon all account it seem the most prudent to carry the girl to Paris to the hand of her own chieftain , Macgregor of Bohaldie , who would be very willing to help his kinswoman , on the one hand , and not at all anxious to dishonour James upon other . 

 we make but a slow journey of it up , for Catriona be not so good at the riding as the running , and have scarce sit in the saddle since the Forty - five . but we make it out at last , reach Paris early of a Sabbath morning , and make all speed , under Alan s guidance , to find Bohaldie . he be finely lodge , and live in a good style , have a pension on the Scots Fund , as well as private mean ; greet Catriona like one of his own house , and seem altogether very civil and discreet , but not particularly open . we ask of the news of James More . " Poor James ! " say he , and shake his head and smile , so that I think he know far than he mean to tell . then we show he Palliser s letter , and he draw a long face at that . 

 " Poor James ! " say he again . " well , there be bad folk than James More , too . but this be dreadful bad . tut , tut , he must have forget himself entirely ! this be a most undesirable letter . but , for all that , gentleman , I can not see what we would want to make it public for . it s an ill bird that foul his own nest , and we be all scot folk and all Hieland . " 

 upon this we all agree , save perhaps Alan ; and still more upon the question of our marriage , which Bohaldie take in his own hand , as though there have be no such person as James More , and give Catriona away with very pretty manner and agreeable compliment in French . it be not till all be over , and our health drunk , that he tell we James be in that city , whither he have precede we some day , and where he now lie sick , and like to die . I think I see by my wife s face what way her inclination point . 

 " and let we go see he , then , " say I. 

 " if it be your pleasure , " say Catriona . these be early day . 

 he be lodge in the same quarter of the city with his chief , in a great house upon a corner ; and we be guide up to the garret where he lie by the sound of Highland piping . it seem he have just borrow a set of they from Bohaldie to amuse his sickness ; though he be no such hand as be his brother Rob , he make good music of the kind ; and it be strange to observe the french folk crowd on the stair , and some of they laugh . he lie prop in a pallet . the first look of he I see he be upon his last business ; and , doubtless , this be a strange place for he to die in . but even now I find I can scarce dwell upon his end with patience . Doubtless , Bohaldie have prepare he ; he seem to know we be marry , compliment we on the event , and give we a benediction like a patriarch . 

 " I have be never understand , " say he . " I forgive you both without an afterthought ; " after which he speak for all the world in his old manner , be so obliging as to play we a tune or two upon his pipe , and borrow a small sum before I leave . 

 I could not trace even a hint of shame in any part of his behaviour ; but he be great upon forgiveness ; it seem always fresh to he . I think he forgive I every time we meet ; and when after some four day he pass away in a kind of odour of affectionate sanctity , I could have tear my hair out for exasperation . I have he bury ; but what to put upon his tomb be quite beyond I , till at last I consider the date would look well alone . 

 I think it wise to resign all thought of Leyden , where we have appear once as brother and sister , and it would certainly look strange to return in a new character . Scotland would be do for we ; and thither , after I have recover that which I have leave behind , we sail in a Low Country ship . 

 
 and now , Miss Barbara Balfour   to set the lady first , and Mr. Alan Balfour young of Shaws , here be the story bring fairly to an end . a great many of the folk that take a part in it , you will find   if you think well   that you have see and speak with . Alison Hastie in Limekilns be the lass that rock your cradle when you be too small to know of it , and walk abroad with you in the policy when you be big . that very fine great lady that be Miss Barbara s name - mamma be no other than the same Miss Grant that make so much a fool of David Balfour in the house of the Lord Advocate . and I wonder whether you remember a little , lean , lively gentleman in a scratch - wig and a wraprascal , that come to Shaws very late of a dark night , and whom you be awaken out of your bed and bring down to the dining - hall to be present to , by the name of Mr. Jamieson ? or have Alan forget what he do at Mr. Jamieson s request a most disloyal act for which , by the letter of the law , he might be hang no less than drink the king s health across the water ? these be strange doing in a good Whig house ! but Mr. Jamieson be a man privileged , and might set fire to my corn - barn ; and the name they know he by now in France be the Chevalier Stewart . 

 as for Davie and Catriona , I shall watch you pretty close in the next day , and see if you be so bold as to be laugh at papa and mamma . it be true we be not so wise as we might have be , and make a great deal of sorrow out of nothing ; but you will find as you grow up that even the artful Miss Barbara , and even the valiant Mr. Alan , will be not so very much wise than their parent . for the life of man upon this world of ours be a funny business . they talk of the angel weep ; but I think they must more often be hold their side as they look on ; and there be one thing I determine to do when I begin this long story , and that be to tell out everything as it befell .
